# 16 — Dispatcher Backlog

Working backlog for items extracted from `input/input_raw.md`. Each row
points to the originating line range so context is recoverable.

**Convention:** items are dispatched in rounds; each round runs as one
or more parallel sub-agents on the
`claude/implement-input-raw-changes-2WiOF` branch (or worktree of it).
Status legend:

- `queued` — vetted, waiting for dispatch slot
- `in-progress` — agent is working (note round + agent ID/branch)
- `done` — landed in this branch (commit hash)
- `blocked` — needs user input (note reason)
- `parked` — out of scope for this branch (e.g. dataship work, infra)

## Scope filter

`input_raw.md` mixes work for at least three projects:

1. `dlr-shepard/shepard` (this repo, Java/Quarkus backend + Nuxt 3 / Vue 3 /
   Vuetify 3 frontend + client libs) — **in scope**. (Earlier rounds said
   "Angular"; corrected by the `aidocs/33` agent which verified against
   `frontend/package.json:24,45-46`.)
2. `dlr-shepard/shepard-dataship` (separate Python client; M1–M9 milestones
   on lines 975–1214 reference `src/ui/*.py`, `src/worker.py`, etc.) —
   **out of scope here**, parked.
3. Program-level work (HMC, federation, project website, AAS) — **parked**,
   not implementable from this repo.

## Backlog (this repo only)

| PM1b3 | True runtime CDI integration — a vendor drops `shepard-plugin-foo-x.y.z.jar` into `/deployments/plugins/` at runtime and its REST endpoints + admin CLI subcommand come up **without** declaring the plugin in the backend's `with-plugins` Maven profile. Option B (per the `aidocs/69` analysis): extend `PluginContext` with `registerHttpRoute(pathPattern, handler)` so plugins ship Vert.x handlers instead of `@Path` resources (side-steps Quarkus's build-time CDI scanning); wire `PluginRegistry` to a singleton `PluginRouter` that manages the live Vert.x route table. PM1b2's `DEGRADED` state becomes the auto-detection signal: a JAR-walk plugin without a matching `quarkus.index-dependency.*` config key lands DEGRADED with `plugin.runtime.no-cdi-scan` and the failureMessage points at the runbook. | IX1 | External-service minimal-instance infrastructure — prefer running **the real service in a minimal Docker container** over synthetic WireMock stubs; stubs only for services with no self-hostable open-source image. Target list and preferred image for each: (a) **Helmholtz Databus + MOSS** (`R1/MB1`) — Apache Jena Fuseki testcontainer (`stain/jena-fuseki`) is the actual SPARQL store Databus uses; MOSS indexer gets a real minimal MOSS module config pointed at it; validates the full SHACL + DCAT round-trip against real SPARQL semantics. (b) **AAS Registry** (`AAS1-reg`) — `eclipsebasyx/aas-environment:2.x` official image; exercises the real BaSyx REST wire shape including `AssetAdministrationShell` registration payloads. (c) **Matrix home server** (`MTX1a`) — `matrixdotorg/synapse:latest` or `conduit` minimal testcontainer; real `/_matrix/client/v3` routes so the notification flow is exercised against actual Matrix protocol. (d) **Open3D sidecar** (`PC1b`, `VID2a`) — real image we build from `infrastructure/sidecar-open3d/`; testcontainered directly via the built image tag. (e) **SA-Python bridge** (`SA1`) — if the bridge is an HTTP microservice we control, testcontainer it directly; SA COM itself is not CI-testable (Windows-only), so the CI test validates the bridge's HTTP contract against a fixture PLY file. (f) **Helmholtz Unhide HKG harvester** (`UH1`) — no official self-hostable harvester image; use a minimal WireMock container (`wiremock/wiremock:3`) that calls back our feed URL and verifies the JSON-LD shape. (g) **DataCite** (`KIP1d`) — no self-hostable Fabrica; CI falls back to `api.test.datacite.org` OR a WireMock stub set for `/dois` CRUD + `/heartbeat`. (h) **ePIC handle service** (`KIP1c`) — no self-hostable image; WireMock stub for `POST /api/handles/{prefix}/{suffix}`. Pattern: `ExternalServiceStack` Quarkus test-resource (`@QuarkusTestResource`) accepts a `services` init-arg; each enum value starts the correct Testcontainer or WireMock map; `infrastructure-local/docker-compose.external-services.yml` exposes the same images for local dev and manual integration runs without test framework overhead. | user request 2026-05-16 | L | **design sketch** | DX1 (`ShepardTestStack`) handles internal DBs; IX1 handles outbound integrations. Both needed before external integrations land in CI proper. Sub-IDs: IX1a (`ExternalServiceStack` skeleton + Fuseki/Databus), IX1b (BaSyx AAS testcontainer), IX1c (Matrix/Synapse testcontainer), IX1d (Open3D sidecar testcontainer), IX1e (WireMock fallbacks for DataCite + ePIC + Unhide), IX1f (SA-Python HTTP bridge testcontainer). |

| N1b | Pre-seeded common ontologies (PROV-O / Dublin Core / schema.org / FOAF / QUDT / OM-2 / W3C Time / GeoSPARQL) bundled at `backend/src/main/resources/ontologies/`. SHA-256 pinning. Idempotent re-import. | — | M | **shipped** | `OntologySeedService` reads `ontologies-manifest.json` from classpath, verifies SHA-256 per file, calls `n10s.rdf.import.inline` (n10s `import.fetch` does not accept `classpath:` URIs). Wired into `N10sBootstrapHook.run()` after the constraint step. Two new config keys: `shepard.semantic.internal.preseed-ontologies.enabled=true` (default on; ADR-0019 records the rationale) + `shepard.semantic.internal.preseed-ontologies.skip-bundles=` (CSV; e.g. `qudt,om-2`). Fail-soft per-bundle — a missing classpath file, SHA mismatch, or n10s call error is logged and the next bundle is attempted. The bundled `.ttl` files are minimum-viable Turtle stubs carrying each ontology's canonical IRI prefix and a handful of representative classes/properties; full canonical content lands when an operator runs the N1c refresh CLI (or replaces a file and regenerates the manifest entry by hand). ~16 KB of bundled stubs today; the full ~13 MB target lands with N1c. |
| N1c | `shepard-admin semantic refresh-ontologies` CLI per `aidocs/22 §4.x`. | — | S | **shipped** | New backend endpoint `POST /v2/admin/semantic/refresh-ontologies` (instance-admin gated) drives a new `OntologyRefreshService` that walks the bundled-ontology manifest, fetches each bundle's pinned `canonicalUrl`, recomputes SHA-256, and re-imports via `n10s.rdf.import.inline` when the hash differs (or when `force=true`). Best-effort per bundle — partial failures land in the `errors[]` array with 200 OK overall, mirroring the seed service's fail-soft stance from `aidocs/48`. New CLI command `shepard-admin semantic refresh-ontologies [--bundles=prov-o,qudt] [--force]` wraps it; human-table + JSON output; exit 0 on success / 1 on any per-bundle error. No new config keys (reuses the `shepard.semantic.internal.*` namespace). Backend coverage: `OntologyRefreshService` 87% line / 74% branch, `SemanticAdminRest` 100% line / 92% branch; CLI command 92% line / 92% branch. |

Read-only gate: SELECT + ASK allowed; CONSTRUCT / INSERT / DELETE / UPDATE / DROP / CREATE / LOAD / CLEAR / ADD / MOVE / COPY rejected 400 `sparql.read-only` via `SparqlQueryValidator`. Type dispatch: `INTERNAL` → n10s HTTP at `POST /rdf/neo4j/sparql` on port 7474 (Basic auth from existing `neo4j.username`/`neo4j.password`; configurable via `shepard.semantic.internal.http-url`); `SPARQL` → proxy external endpoint GET `?query=`; `JSKOS`/`SKOSMOS` → 501 `sparql.not-supported`. Response: upstream body passed through verbatim with `Content-Type: application/sparql-results+json`; non-200 upstream → 502/503 RFC 7807. `SemanticRepositoryDAO.findByAppId` added (mirrors TimeseriesReferenceDAO pattern). Two test classes: `SparqlQueryValidatorTest` (37 cases, keyword + edge-case coverage), `SemanticSparqlRestTest` (21 cases, 401/404/400/501/200 gates). ### Newly surfaced (second-pass analysis of `input_raw.md` lines 1840–8409)

These come from a re-read of regions the first scan missed. `R7` deduplicates with existing `L1`. `R2` (RO-Crate) is **already implemented** in this repo (`ExportConstants.ROCRATE_METADATA`); only the per-payload selection enhancement remains. Most others are blocked on user/maintainer decisions.

| ID | Item | input_raw refs | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| R1 | Databus + MOSS federation layer (`shepard-plugin-databus`) | 8380 | M | **design done** | `aidocs/77`. Full design: `:DatabusConfig` admin entity, admin REST + CLI parity, researcher-facing `POST /v2/collections/{appId}/publish/databus`, PROV-O Turtle generation, `shepard` MOSS module definition (SHACL + indexer). MB1a–MB1g phasing. Gated on PROV1a (`:Activity` capture, `aidocs/55`) and the MOSS module YAML landing in the DLR-internal Databus instance. |
| R2 | Per-payload selective RO-Crate export (refinement of existing export) | 8381 | S–M | **Phase 1 done** | Round 6, commit `be0eb26` (cherry-picked). Existing exporter lives in `backend/src/main/java/de/dlr/shepard/context/export/` (`ExportService` is the walker entry point, `ExportBuilder` wraps `edu.kit.datamanager.ro_crate.RoCrate.RoCrateBuilder`). Phase 1 adds an optional `ExportSelection` body on a **new** sibling `POST /collections/{collectionId}/export` (the existing GET is preserved unchanged for byte-identical legacy behaviour). Selection has two sections: `payloads` (`include` allow-list of kinds + `excludeIds` deny-list) and `metadata` booleans (permissions / annotations / labJournal / versions / subscriptions). The selection actually applied is recorded as a JSON block on the root data entity in `ro-crate-metadata.json` so consumers can tell what was excluded. 18 tests pass (5 new selection-service + 2 new manifest-injection + 11 pre-existing). **Important:** the exporter today does **not** yet emit `permissions / versions / subscriptions / annotations` documents — the booleans are wired and recorded but bundling those metadata kinds is deferred to **R2d**. |
| R2b | File- and column-level selection on payloads (per-FileReference oid include list; per-TimeseriesReference column / time-window picks) | — | M | done | Round 6, commit `60a3ea1`. Adds `payloads.perPayload: Map<entityId, PerPayloadSelection>` and `payloads.strictPerPayload: boolean`. `PerPayloadSelection` has optional `fileOids`, `columns`, `timeRange{start,end}` — kind-applicability is silent (wrong-kind entries ignored). Existing per-OID file-fetch service reused; existing `fieldFilterSet` parameter on `TimeseriesReferenceService.exportReferencedTimeseriesByShepardId` covers per-column projection; a new 14-arg overload accepts `startNanosOverride` / `endNanosOverride` for time-window without mutating the reference. Stale OIDs / unknown columns silently skipped + recorded in a new `selection.warnings[]` array on the manifest's root selection block; `strictPerPayload=true` flips that to 400. 11 new tests pass (43/43 export-package). P17b lint stays green. |
| R2c | Per-payload metadata-field redaction (e.g. include the annotation but redact its label) | — | M | done | Round 6, commit `f993e8b`. Adds `metadata.redactFields: Set<RedactableField>` to `ExportSelection`. **Closed enum** of 6 fields, each verified against the actual IO type before shipping (one stop-and-report adjustment): `PERMISSION_USERNAME` (replaces `owner` + `reader[]` + `writer[]` + `manager[]`), `PERMISSION_GROUP_IDS` (empties `readerGroupIds` / `writerGroupIds` — renamed from proposed `…_GROUP_NAME` because `PermissionsIO` carries group ids only), `ANNOTATION_LABEL` (replaces `propertyName` — proposed `label` doesn't exist; IRI left intact as stable id), `ANNOTATION_VALUE` (replaces `valueName` — proposed `value` doesn't exist), `VERSION_AUTHOR` (replaces `createdBy` — no `author` field), `LAB_JOURNAL_CONTENT` (replaces `journalContent`). Mutation is direct setter on the Lombok `@Data` IO types before serialisation. Manifest selection block records the **set** but not the replacement values (no leak vector). 11 new tests pass; 54/54 export-package total. |
| R2d | Emit permissions / versions / subscriptions / semantic-annotations documents from the exporter (the metadata booleans from R2 Phase 1 are wired but the exporter currently doesn't bundle these doc kinds) | — | M | **mostly done** | Round 6, commit `d5fa03c`. **3 of 4 kinds wired:** `permissions` (via `PermissionsService.getPermissionsOfEntityOptional`), `versions` (via `VersionService.getAllVersions`; collection-only — only Collections are versioned), `annotations` (via `BasicEntity.getAnnotations()`). Defaults remain `false` so today's behaviour is unchanged. 14 new tests pass on merged branch (10 service-level in `ExportMetadataBundleTest`, 4 builder-level in `ExportBuilderSelectionTest`). **`subscriptions` deferred** — see **R2d2** below. |
| R2d2 | Emit per-entity subscriptions in the RO-Crate export — needs a URL-pattern → entity-URL matcher because subscriptions in shepard are URL-pattern-based, not per-entity-attached | — | M | done | Round 6, commit `967fbf5`. New `SubscriptionMatcher` extracted from `SubscriptionFilter` (pure refactor; `SubscriptionFilterTest` 7/7 pass); new `EntityUrlSynthesiser` produces canonical paths for Collection / DataObject / BasicReference / LabJournalEntry using the same `Constants.*` tokens the JAX-RS resources use. Walker hook calls `subscriptionService.getMatchingSubscriptionsForUrl(url, method)` and writes `<id>-subscriptions.json` per entity. **Documented trade-off:** subscription patterns are full-URL regexes (scheme + host); export only knows the path, so authors of host-anchored patterns may need a `.*` prefix to also match exports. 7 new tests pass; 43+ on merged branch. |

### API critique series (from `aidocs/23`, 2026-05-05)

The MVP "minimum-viable clunkiness fix" is **P5 + P6 + P7 + P10 + P12 + P16 + P18** (≈ 2 sprints).

| ID | Item | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| P5 | Replace path-segment switching in `PermissionsService.isAllowed` with annotation-based authz on each handler | M | queued | **Same proposal as F1** in `aidocs/24`. Use F1 as the canonical ID; P5 is its API-critique counterpart. |
| P6 | Fold `X-API-KEY` into `Authorization: Bearer`, deprecate the second header | S | queued | Breaking; bundles with P4 versioning. |
| P7 | Ship the unified `POST /search/v2` from `aidocs/13 §2`; deprecate the five legacy search routes | L | queued | Maps to epic E2 in `aidocs/20`. **Gated on C5** (Cypher injection). |
| P8 | Polymorphic `/annotations` endpoint replacing the four per-kind annotation rests | M | queued | Depends on `aidocs/14` model unification. |
| P9 | Single `/entities/{kind}/{id}/permissions` route replacing per-container permissions endpoints | M | queued | Overlaps **A2**. |
| P10 | `POST /sql/timeseries` curated SQL-over-HTTP for bulk reads — **answers the "timeseries to Excel" prompt** | M | **design done** | New paradigm slice; design landed in `aidocs/platform/29-p10-implementation-design.md`. JSON DSL request body (vs raw SQL or templated lang). Cypher-first permission flow via `filterAllowedForUser` (post-P2). Three-format content negotiation (`text/csv` default, `application/json`, `application/x-ndjson`; Arrow deferred to P11). 1M-row + PT60S caps; mandatory time range. **Gated on C5.** Spawns **P10a** (S, JSON-only behind feature flag), **P10b** (M, CSV+NDJSON streaming, caps), **P10c** (S, default-on, wrapper retarget). |
| P10a | Phase 1: `SqlQuerySpec` + `SqlQueryCompiler` + JSON-only endpoint behind `shepard.timeseries.sql.enabled=false` | — | S | **✓ shipped** | `POST /v2/sql/timeseries`. `de.dlr.shepard.data.timeseries.sql` package: `SqlQuerySpec` record, `AllowedTable`/`AllowedColumn` enums, `SqlQueryCompiler` (alias-regex validation, all user values as `?` params), `SqlQueryExecutor` (AgroalDataSource, fetchSize 10k), `JsonWriter`, `PreparedStatementSpec` record, `SqlTimeseriesRest` (with `executeQuery()` package-private method for testability). Feature flag `shepard.timeseries.sql.enabled=false` (default off). 3 test classes: `SqlQueryCompilerTest`, `SqlTimeseriesInjectionTest`, `SqlTimeseriesPermissionTest`; 14 tests pass in standalone JUnit runner. Config keys: `shepard.timeseries.sql.enabled=false`, `…max-rows=1000000`. |
| P10b | Phase 2: `text/csv` + `application/x-ndjson` content negotiation; streaming output with row + duration caps; `Trailer: x-shepard-truncated` | — | M | **✓ shipped** | `CsvWriter` (RFC 4180, CRLF, double-quote escaping, ISO-8601 timestamps, UTF-8 no BOM) + `NdjsonWriter` (one JSON object per line, `\n` delimiter) added. `JsonWriter.write()` return type changed to `WriteResult`. `SqlQueryExecutor` refactored: `executeJson`/`executeCsv`/`executeNdjson` each take `OutputStream` and return `WriteResult`; `Statement.cancel()` called on `IOException` (client disconnect); `statement_timeout` set per request via `SET statement_timeout = N`. `SqlTimeseriesRest` gains content negotiation via `@HeaderParam("Accept")` (CSV default for `*/*`; JSON; NDJSON), `@Context HttpServerResponse` for VertX trailer emission, `@ConfigProperty` wiring for `max-rows` and `max-duration`. New config key: `shepard.timeseries.sql.max-duration=PT60S`. `Content-Disposition: attachment; filename="timeseries.csv"` on CSV responses. `Trailer: x-shepard-truncated` announcement header; `x-shepard-truncated: true` trailer via `HttpServerResponse.putTrailer()` on row-cap hit. New test class: `SqlTimeseriesFormatTest` (writer unit tests: RFC 4180 quoting, null fields, row cap, NDJSON per-line, format negotiation, REST-layer routing, trailer emission verified via Mockito-mocked `HttpServerResponse`). `WriteResult` record added. `QueryTimeoutExceptionMapper` (`@Provider ExceptionMapper`) maps SQLState 57014 to HTTP 504. Admin-config deferral resolved in P10c. `docs/reference/timeseries-reference.md` created. |
| P10c | Phase 3: feature flag default-on; `:SqlTimeseriesConfig` + `GET/PATCH /v2/admin/sql-timeseries/config` runtime config for `max-rows` and `max-duration` | — | S–M | **✓ shipped** | `:SqlTimeseriesConfig` Neo4j singleton (A3b pattern) seeded from deploy-time defaults on first start; `GET/PATCH /v2/admin/sql-timeseries/config` `@RolesAllowed("instance-admin")`; runtime value wins over `application.properties` deploy-time default (`effectiveMaxRows()` / `effectiveMaxDurationIso()` in `SqlTimeseriesConfigService`). `SqlTimeseriesRest` now reads effective caps from `SqlTimeseriesConfigService` (removes direct `@ConfigProperty` injection). `V43__Add_appId_constraint_SqlTimeseriesConfig.cypher` migration adds `REQUIRE n.appId IS UNIQUE`. Feature flag `shepard.timeseries.sql.enabled` flipped to `true` (default-on). 13 unit tests (`SqlTimeseriesConfigRestTest`: GET defaults, GET patched, PATCH only-maxRows, PATCH only-maxDuration, PATCH null clears, PATCH zero maxRows → 400, PATCH negative maxRows → 400, PATCH invalid maxDuration → 400, PATCH empty-string maxDuration → 400, annotation gate, path, no-op null body, valid duration → 200). Existing tests (`SqlTimeseriesPermissionTest`, `SqlTimeseriesFormatTest`) updated to stub `configService` instead of direct field assignment. **Follow-up (CLI parity):** `shepard-admin sql-timeseries {status,set-max-rows,set-max-duration}` deferred to a follow-up slice (same pattern as ROR1 CLI parity shipped separately). Note: V42 (`InstanceRorConfig` constraint) was referenced in the ROR1 commit message but the file was not committed to disk — gap surfaced here; MigrationsRunner tolerates version gaps so no runtime breakage, but the file should be retroactively created before V44 ships. |

New `TimeseriesNdjsonService` reads request as `BufferedReader`, validates each `{timestamp, value}` line independently (timeseries identity supplied as query params), batches 5000 lines per `insertManyDataPointsWithCopyCommand` call. Streams response (per-line errors + `{"summary": {"accepted": A, "rejected": R, "durationMs": D}}` final line). Caps: `shepard.timeseries.ingest.ndjson.batch-size` (default 5000), `…max-duration` (default PT5M). Auth check happens **before** stream consumption. 5 `@QuarkusComponentTest` cases pass: mixed valid/invalid, multi-chunk streaming proof, exact-batch-count assertion (12000 lines → 3 batches), pre-stream auth failure. **Follow-up:** once P3's `insertManyDataPointsWithCopyCommandBatched` is preferred, swap the service-layer batching for the repository-layer one. |

Strategy choice: ship PATCH additively in `/v1/` and deprecate the partial-PUT semantics in `/v2/` (cleanest of three). Done so far: pilot **`Collection`** (`10531bd`), **`DataObject`** (`fd7ea76`), **`LabJournalEntry`** (`f0b3bd3` + canonicalisation). | P21-References-prereq | **Architectural finding:** the `*ReferenceRest` family (`BasicReference`, `CollectionReference`, `DataObjectReference`, `FileReference`, `SpatialDataReference`, `StructuredDataReference`, `TimeseriesReference`, `URIReference`) has **no `@PUT` for entity metadata** — same shape as P21-File-prereq. References are create-only-then-delete in the current model. | — | M | **needs decision** | Same call as P21-File-prereq: should references be metadata-editable post-creation? | P21-File-prereq | **Architectural finding (P21-File agent stop-and-report):** the entire `data/` container family (`FileRest`, `StructuredDataRest`, `SpatialDataPointRest`, `TimeseriesRest`) has **no `@PUT` for entity metadata** — only `@PUT /{id}/permissions`. None of the `*ContainerService` classes expose an `updateContainer` method. PATCH on those resources is blocked on a prior decision: should data containers be metadata-editable post-creation, or stay create-only-then-delete? | — | M | **needs decision** | If yes, ship `PUT /<container>/{id}` first (for each of File / StructuredData / SpatialData / TimeseriesContainer), then the P21 PATCH follow-ons land trivially. If no, the PATCH follow-ons for the data family are formally out of scope and `aidocs/26` finding #1 is partially closed — the data containers are *deliberately* immutable. |

| P23 | Presign-vs-cache TTL invariant validator — bound presigned-URL TTL by `shepard.permissions.cache.ttl` so a permission revoked while a URL is live cannot keep granting access | S | **done** | `PresignTtlValidator` (`@ApplicationScoped`): reads `shepard.storage.presign.{upload,download,export}-ttl` (defaults PT15M/PT5M/PT30M) + `shepard.permissions.cache.ttl` (default PT5M); caps each effective TTL to the cache TTL; emits `WARN` at startup when a configured TTL is capped. | F3 | Permission audit log (Postgres table) for grants/revokes | S–M | **✓ shipped** | `V1.10.0__add_permission_audit_log_table.sql` — `permission_audit_log` table (BIGSERIAL PK, TIMESTAMPTZ, entity_app_id, entity_kind, actor_username, action, detail_json). `PermissionAuditLogService` (ApplicationScoped, AgroalDataSource, fire-and-forget). Hooked into all three write paths in `PermissionsService`: `createPermissions` → GRANT, `updatePermissionsByNeo4jId` → UPDATE (before/after JSON), `deletePermissions` → REVOKE. `GET /v2/admin/permission-audit/log` (`@RolesAllowed("instance-admin")`, params: entityAppId, actor, from, to ISO-8601, page/size). 13 new unit tests. |
| F4 | Versioned cache invalidation key: `(entityId, AccessType, userSub, jwtIat)` | S | **✓ shipped** | Changed `isAccessTypeAllowedForUser` signature from 3-arg to 4-arg; 4th arg `jwtIat` is the JWT `iat` claim (seconds-since-epoch, default `0L` when no JWT or no iat). `JWTPrincipal` gained an `iat` field; `JWTFilter.parsePrincipalFromAccessToken()` extracts `body.getIssuedAt()`. Services with `AuthenticationContext` pass `currentIat()` (reads `authenticationContext.getPrincipal().getIat()`); REST resources and the cache warmer without live-request context pass `0L`. `CompositeCacheKey` now 4-tuple. 4 new `PermissionsServiceIatCacheKeyTest` tests. |
| F5 | Explicit fail-closed invariant when Neo4j is degraded | S | **✓ shipped** | Added `dbHealthRegistry.isCurrentlyDown(DatabaseKind.NEO4J)` guard at the top of `PermissionsService.isAllowed()`: returns `false` immediately when Neo4j is DOWN without calling the DAO. Null-safe (guards against `@InjectMocks` test environments). 3 new `PermissionsServiceNeo4jGuardTest` tests covering: DOWN returns false without DAO call; UP does not short-circuit; guard is independent of username. |
| F6 | Design F1's seam so a future OPA / Cedar `PolicyDecisionPoint` is a drop-in | XS (within F1) | queued | **Verdict from `aidocs/24`:** No to OPA/Cedar adoption now (overkill for a single Quarkus service with small graph-shaped policy); yes to making the seam future-proof at half-day cost. |
| F7 | Row-level security in TimescaleDB / PostGIS — denormalise ACLs into the data DBs | L | parked — conditions for unparking listed in `aidocs/24` | **Verdict:** No for v1. Backend is the only enforcement point; replicating ACLs into Postgres adds a second source of truth with no current threat-model justification. Conditions for a flip: more than one client bypasses the backend, or read fanout becomes the dominant cost. |
| F8 | Configurable OIDC roles-claim path (`shepard.oidc.roles-claim-path`, default `realm_access.roles`); `JWTFilter` walks the dot-path so non-Keycloak IdPs (Pocket ID, Authentik, Azure AD) can carry roles in their native claim shape | XS-S | **done** | Bundled with **A0** (`2901834`). `shepard.instance-admin.role` (default empty = no IdP-side admin) names the role-string within the claim that maps to `instance-admin`. CONFIG-status row in `aidocs/34`. |

## Open user decisions (blocking some items)

1. **Leaked JWTs** at `aidocs/input/input_raw.md:222` and `:360` (issuers
   `bt-au-cube2.intra.dlr.de`, `bt-au-cube3.intra.dlr.de`, sub `kreb_fl`).
   Already on `origin`. Need: rotate tokens, decide whether to redact in
   the file, and whether to rewrite history.
2. ~~**API versioning (P4)** is breaking — confirm strategy
   (`/shepard/api/v1` prefix, dual-serve, deprecation window) before
   dispatching.~~ — **resolved**: shipped non-breaking. Upstream
   `/shepard/api/...` stays byte-frozen via explicit class-level
   `@Path("/shepard/api/...")` prefix; new fork-additive endpoints land
   under `/v2/` (per `CLAUDE.md` API-version policy). User-facing URLs
   unchanged.
3. **Templates system (L3)** is large and design-heavy — needs a written
   design before implementation.
4. **Neo4J ID migration (L2)** is large and touches a lot of code — needs
   a written design before implementation.
5. **Admin role mechanism (A0)** — A3b discovered there is no admin auth
   in shepard today. JWT roles are always `new String[0]`, so
   `@RolesAllowed("admin")` denies everyone. Three paths offered:
   (a) full admin-role mechanism populating roles from OIDC claims
   (~50 lines + config), (b) dev-profile-only exposure of admin
   endpoints, (c) scope-shift admin endpoints to `/temp/admin/*` with
   the same auth as the existing `/temp/migrations/*` carve-out and
   harden later. Affects A3b, P3c.
6. **R-series items (R1–R9)** from the second-pass input analysis are
   mostly blocked on design / framework / asset decisions — see
   "Newly surfaced" table.

### Round 1 — 2026-05-05

Dispatched two small, well-isolated agents in parallel worktrees.
Their output lands as separate commits on this branch.

| ID | Agent description | Status | Commit | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| A1 | Bounded-timeout DB connection wait with exponential backoff | done | `a74d278` | Replaces infinite loops in `MigrationsRunner.waitForConnection` and `NeoConnector`. Adds `ConnectionWaitTimeoutException`, 5-test `MigrationsRunnerTest` (deterministic via injected clock+sleeper). Spawned follow-ups A1d, A1e. |
| A4 | Caffeine-backed permission cache with TTL/LRU | done | `53996a3` | Cache was already Caffeine via `quarkus-cache`; landed per-cache TTL/max-size config + 5-test behavioural contract. Spawned follow-ups A4c (warming), A4d (metrics). |

**Round 1 outcome:** both items landed cleanly on the dispatcher branch.
A1 + A4 land 357 lines added across 7 files (5 prod, 2 test) with 9 new
unit tests, all passing. Two stale assumptions in `input_raw.md` were
corrected on the way (A1: the analysis flagged Mongo/Timescale/PostGIS
infinite waits, but only Neo4j had them in this codebase; A4: the
permission cache was already Caffeine-backed, not a basic Map).

### Round 2 — 2026-05-05

Dispatched 5 agents in parallel worktrees. P3, A1b, and A1e all sit in
the migrations / startup / health area, so cherry-pick conflicts are
possible — explicit non-overlap clauses included in each prompt:

- A1e owns `MigrationsRunner.java` (just the catch blocks).
- A1b owns health-check classes; explicitly told **not** to touch
  `MigrationsRunner` / `NeoConnector` / Neo4j common.
- P3 owns the InfluxDB→TimescaleDB migration tool (separate module);
  expected to be disjoint from A1b/A1e.

L5 (API keys) and A3 (feature toggles) are independent of all of the above.

**Round 2 outcome:** all 5 items landed on the dispatcher branch.
~3,200 lines added across ~60 files, **102 new unit tests** all passing
on the merged branch (8 `MigrationsRunner` + 21 health-check + 9 API-key
+ 2 versioning toggle + 17 migration progress + 5 from earlier round +
existing regressions). Two cherry-pick conflicts resolved manually:
- `MigrationsRunnerTest.java` (A1 vs A1e — combined test sets).
- `application.properties` (A1 vs A3 — kept both new keys).
Three stale spots in `input_raw.md` were corrected during dispatch:
- A1: only Neo4j had infinite waits, not Mongo/Timescale/PostGIS.
- A4: cache was already Caffeine, not a basic Map.
- P3: orchestrator image source lives outside this repo; only the
  COPY path was instrumentable here.

| `aidocs/platform/20-epic-roadmap.md` | 14-epic catalogue with Mermaid dependency graph + 2-track 6-month plan | done | `fc4ae3b` |
| `aidocs/archive/21-user-interest-gauge.md` | Demand signals for HDF5/HSDS, tabular, KG interfaces + survey plan | done | `362712e` |
| `aidocs/ops/22-admin-cli-draft.md` | Candidate functions for a future `shepard-admin` CLI | done | `452eded` |

**Key findings from these docs that should drive Round 4 priorities:**

- **`aidocs/19` flags two security fragilities at the top:**
  - **C3 fallback** at `PermissionsService.java:262+` — when the
    permissions node is missing, the fallback grants Reader+Writer+Manager.
    This is a full-access backdoor catalogued in
    `aidocs/archive/07-security-issues.md` C3 — **not new, but not yet fixed**.
  - **C5 Cypher injection** at `Neo4jQueryBuilder.java:198-244` —
    string-concatenated query construction; cross-cuts every search
    endpoint and gates `aidocs/semantics/13-search-improvements.md`.
  - Plus **A0** (admin role) — already in our backlog.
- **`aidocs/20` recommends two parallel tracks:**
  - **Foundations track:** E1 (foundations: A0 + observability + P4 + L6 + S1) → E5 (streaming + ID alignment) → E11 (permissions + admin CLI) → E2 (unified search v2).
  - **User-value track:** E12 (UX & ecosystem) → E6 (annotation generalisation) → E9 (spatial graduate/deprecate) → E4 (triplestore + SPARQL).
  - Three "could start tomorrow" epics: **E1, E5, E12**.
  - Three "blocked on user decision" epics: **E14** (Neo4j ID migration owner), **E9** (spatial graduate vs deprecate), **E4** (default ontology + reasoning profile + n10s deployment).
- **`aidocs/21` ranks the three candidate development directions:**
  - **KG interfaces:** strongest evidence (4 open GitLab issues, partial `SparqlConnector` already, two independent user groups). Ready to act once #274 unblocks.
  - **HDF5/HSDS:** low-medium; one named asker, no GitLab issue, TimescaleDB satisfies the temporal subset. **Maintainer-confirmed hard constraint (2026-05-05):** any HDF5 surface must be compatible with the existing Python ecosystem (`h5py` / `PyTables` / `pandas.read_hdf`) — `h5pyd` over HSDS is the canonical access path; "download original file" is the fallback. Recorded in epic E7 (`aidocs/platform/20-epic-roadmap.md:309-329`) and §3.6 of `aidocs/archive/21-user-interest-gauge.md`.
  - **Tabular/relational:** thin; the ask hides two distinct products (interface vs storage). Defer until separated.

## New designs landed in the 2026-05-12 batch (post-A0)

Seven design docs landed (`aidocs/52`..`aidocs/58`), each with its own
phasing. Umbrella rows below; per-doc sub-ID detail lives in the cited
aidoc. **`T1` is hereby redirected to the new `aidocs/54` shape**
(`:ShepardTemplate` first-class entity), superseding the older
`aidocs/39` hack; the old T1 sub-IDs T1a–T1h are renumbered per
`aidocs/54 §9`. **`D1` in `aidocs/58 §5` is renamed `CP1`** to avoid
colliding with the existing in-app-docs D1 series. **`AI1` in
`aidocs/58 §8` is renamed `GR1`** (GraphRAG) to avoid colliding with
the existing `aidocs/43` AI1 umbrella.

| TM1 | Time Reference Model — `timeReference: enum WALL_CLOCK \| EXPERIMENT_RELATIVE` + `wallClockOffset: long` (nanoseconds epoch of t=0 in stored data) on `TimeseriesReference`. Both fields mutable via `PATCH /v2/timeseries-references/{appId}` — offset can be corrected any time a better anchor is discovered (ffprobe, SA sync signal, manual). Translation: `wall_clock_ns(sample) = wallClockOffset + sample_t_ns`. Optional `wallClockOffsetSource: String` tag ("manual" / "ffprobe" / "SA_sync" / "NTP_marker"). V-series Cypher migration backfills `timeReference="WALL_CLOCK"` on all existing rows. Enables SB2a (video+timeseries overlay), SB2d (multi-channel timeline), SB2h (SA 6D tracking sync), and DT1 snapshot timestamp alignment across sources. | VID2 | Camera-to-scene calibration — click-based point-correspondence UI lets a researcher click N paired points (image pixel ↔ CAD/scene world point) to solve the camera extrinsic transform via PnP (OpenCV EPNP+RANSAC; reuses the Open3D sidecar from PC1b). `POST /v2/videos/{videoAppId}/align-to/{cadAppId}` body `{ correspondences: [{imageX, imageY, worldX, worldY, worldZ}], cameraIntrinsics?: [9] }`. User can skip features that are occluded, moving, or unclear — sparse correspondences are fine (min 4, RANSAC-robust above 8). Per-correspondence residual colour feedback (green/yellow/red). Stores `[:CAMERA_ALIGNED_TO { matrix:[16], rmse, correspondenceCount, K:[9], solverAlgorithm, alignedAt }]` on `VideoStream→CadReference`. Unlocks: SB2a CAMERA_FRUSTUM mode (real camera matrix in 3D viewer), 3D annotation → video projection overlay (click annotation → highlight pixel on video), DT1 live camera viewport. Sub-IDs: VID2a (backend PnP + Neo4j edge), VID2b (frontend side-by-side picker UI), VID2c (3D viewer: frustum + projection overlay), VID2d (DT1 camera viewport). | user request 2026-05-16 | L | **design sketch** | VID2a gated on VID1a (video upload) + PC1b sidecar (Open3D). Six rules: `search_threshold_breach` (k6 p95 > 3000ms → Neo4j page-cache), `collections_threshold_breach` (k6 p95 > 800ms → perms-cache), `jvm_heap_too_small` (heap > 85% → -Xmx), `gc_pauses_high` (GC max > 200ms → G1GC), `permissions_cache_cold` (hit rate < 60% → cache size + TTL), `mongo_latency_high` (avg cmd > 50ms → pool size). Prometheus queries for JVM heap, GC pause, perms-cache hit ratio, Mongo latency; falls back gracefully when Prometheus is unreachable. `--json` for machine-readable output; `--output FILE`; `--dry-run` uses canned data. Exit 0 = healthy, exit 1 = suggestions found (CI-friendly), exit 2 = error. |

| KIP1d | DataCite REST adapter — `shepard-plugin-minter-datacite` JAR. Config keys for DOI prefix + DataCite Member credentials + `:DataciteMinterConfig` singleton. | user request 2026-05-13, `aidocs/66 §5(c)` | M | **shipped** | This PR. New module `plugins/minter-datacite/` mirrors `plugins/minter-local/` shape: `DataciteMinterPluginManifest` discovered via `META-INF/services/de.dlr.shepard.plugin.PluginManifest`, JAR built with `provided`-scope backend dep, declared as a `<dependency>` in the backend's `with-plugins` Maven profile, `quarkus.index-dependency.shepard-plugin-minter-datacite.*` ensures Jandex indexing so the `DataciteMinter` `@ApplicationScoped` bean + `DataciteAdminRest` `@Path` resource are discovered at build time. Activated when an operator flips `shepard.publish.minter=datacite` after configuring credentials. Admin-runtime per CLAUDE.md: new `:DataciteMinterConfig` singleton (idiom from A3b + UH1a + N1c2 — single-instance node, `HasAppId`, seed-on-first-start from `shepard.minters.datacite.*` install defaults, runtime PATCH wins). Admin REST under `/v2/admin/minters/datacite/` with five endpoints: `GET/PATCH /config` (RFC 7396 merge-patch, `@RolesAllowed("instance-admin")`), `POST/DELETE /credential` (set / rotate / clear the DataCite Member password — plaintext never echoed, only first-8 hex of SHA-256 fingerprint surfaced), `POST /test-connection` (probes `<apiBaseUrl>/heartbeat` and reports reachable/statusCode/latencyMs). CLI parity: new `shepard-admin minters datacite {status,enable,disable,set-api-url,set-prefix,set-repository-id,set-publisher,set-landing-page-base,set-state,set-password,clear-password,test-connection}` subcommand group via PM1d's `AdminCliCommandProvider` SPI — twelve verbs in a `MintersCommand` → `DataciteCommand` two-level nesting that lets future minter plugins (ePIC, Crossref, …) slot in alongside without colliding on the top-level name. **`set-password` reads stdin / tty only**, never on the command line, so `ps` + shell history can't leak the credential. **Credential at rest**: AES-GCM (256-bit key derived from `shepard.instance.id` + a fixed pepper, GCM-1 prefixed base64-url-no-padding ciphertext) on `:DataciteMinterConfig.passwordCipher`; SHA-256 hex hash on `:passwordHash` (fingerprint display only). The cipher format includes a `gcm1:` prefix marker so a future cipher upgrade can recognise the legacy shape. **Versioned PIDs (KIP1h respect)**: `DataciteMinter` reads `MintRequest.versionNumber()` directly (KIP1h made it a first-class field), encodes as `version: "v<n>"` in the DataCite request body, and adds `relatedIdentifiers: [{ relationType: IsNewVersionOf, ... }]` for n > 1 — plus a back-fill `PUT /dois/<previous>` that stamps the inverse `HasVersion` so the chain renders both ways in DataCite Commons. Previous-PID lookup is delegated to a `PreviousPublicationResolver` interface that defaults to a no-op (test-friendly; production wires it to the in-core `PublicationDAO` via the manifest hook). **Network hardening**: 10s connect + 30s request timeout on the JDK `HttpClient`; one retry on 5xx / network exception with 1s backoff; `MinterException` on second failure (caught by core `PublishService` → 500 `publish.minter.failed`). 4xx is final (no retry). **Resource-type mapping**: shepard's `digitalObjectType` (Dataset / Collection / Software / Text / Image) maps onto DataCite's `resourceTypeGeneral` vocabulary with `Dataset` as the safe default. **Event mapping**: DataCite `event` field set from `defaultState` — `draft`/`registered`/`findable` → `draft`/`register`/`publish`. New tests: 126 cases across 9 classes (`DataciteMinterTest` 30, `DataciteMinterConfigServiceTest` 24, `DataciteAdminRestTest` 17, `DataciteCommandsTest` 22, `CredentialCipherTest` 12, `DataciteIoTest` 7, `MintersAdminCliCommandProviderTest` 5, `DataciteMinterConfigTest` 5, `DataciteMinterPluginManifestTest` 4). Migration: `V33__Add_appId_constraint_DataciteMinterConfig.cypher` (V31 + V32 are taken by KIP1h backfill + PM1e PluginRuntimeOverride). New deploy-time keys (install defaults that seed the singleton on first start): `shepard.minters.datacite.{enabled,api-base-url,handle-prefix,repository-id,publisher,landing-page-base,default-state}`. Password is NOT a deploy-time key (security posture; gitleaks would flag it). Default `api-base-url=https://api.test.datacite.org` (Fabrica test environment). Operator runbook: `docs/reference/minter-datacite.md`. SpotBugs + findsecbugs clean; backend test suite stays at 2350 (no in-tree code change beyond the application.properties install-default keys + the `with-plugins` profile dep block + the index-dependency declaration — the plugin's 126 new tests live in the plugin module). |

| KIP1f | `DELETE /v2/{kind}/{appId}/publish` — retain the `:Publication` row (KIP records are append-only by convention) but mark the entity's most-recent Publication as retired (`digitalObjectMutability: "retired"` flag on the row). | user request 2026-05-13, `aidocs/66 §7` | S | **shipped** | Retire semantics confirmed: "retired" is a shepard-extension value (standard vocabulary is `mutable`/`fixed`/`immutable`; "retired" means "no longer the operator's intent" without implying the bit-stream changed). `Publication` entity grows additive nullable `digitalObjectMutability` property (no Neo4j migration — additive nullable). `PublicationDAO.retireMostRecent(entityAppId)` — Cypher `MATCH ... ORDER BY mintedAt DESC LIMIT 1 SET digitalObjectMutability='retired' RETURN count(p) AS n` — returns boolean for 404 detection without a double round-trip. `PublishService.retire(kind, appId)` maintains layering (REST → Service → DAO). `DELETE /v2/{kind}/{appId}/publish` mirrors POST's auth gate (Write on entity), returns 204 on success, 404+problem-json `publish.publication.not-found` when no Publication exists. - **Code-rename rule:** `feedback_appid_to_shepardid.md` in agent memory — single coordinated rename pass, NOT ad-hoc.
- **Shipped:** L2a (`fec7979`) additive `appId` property; L2b (`796bc11`) backfill; L2c (`f3ca003`) Cypher rewrites. L2d (v2 surface exposes appId) **gated on H4** (now shipped — L2d ready to land).
- **Sibling backlog rows:** task #58 (TS 5-tuple→shepardId), task #123 (Java internal rename, deferred until SHACL substrate lands), task #125 (rename PRs 3-10 sweep).

### DB-OPT — 2026-05-23 (database optimisation against real-world data — POST-IMPORT)

User directive 2026-05-23: *"after import we should do the database optimisation case we have real word data"*. The MFFD ingest is about to populate the multi-substrate stack with the first **real-world-scale** dataset (≈8k DataObjects + their reference graph + tapelaying TS + bridgewelding TS). That's the perfect baseline for benchmark-driven optimisation. Sequencing: import lands → snapshot the post-import state → run the DB-OPT pass against real data → ship the wins. Builds on `### DB — 2026-05-22` inventory + anti-pattern hunt; this section is the **action layer**.

| ID | Slice | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| DB-OPT1 | **Capture the post-import baseline** — once MFFD ingest completes, snapshot every store: Neo4j node + relationship counts per label, Postgres table sizes + index hit-rates, TimescaleDB chunk count + compression ratio, MongoDB collection sizes, PostGIS geometry counts, Garage bucket size. Output: `aidocs/agent-findings/db-baseline-post-mffd.md`. This is the reference point every optimisation is measured against. | S | queued | Blocks DB-OPT2..5. Should run automatically as the final step of the import script's `--verify-imported` flag in a future v15.3. |
| DB-OPT2 | **Hot-path query analysis** — `EXPLAIN ANALYZE` every Postgres query the backend issues on `/v2/collections/{appId}`, `/v2/timeseries-containers/{appId}/timeseries`, `/v2/collections/{appId}/data-objects` against the real MFFD data. Same for Neo4j `PROFILE` of the Cypher analogs. Output: ranked list of queries by latency + plan + suggested index. Wins land as a `V##__add_index_hot_path.{sql,cypher}` migration. | M | queued | Real-world data is the only honest signal here; synthetic LUMEN data has wrong cardinality. |
| DB-OPT3 | **Timeseries-specific tuning** — TimescaleDB chunk interval vs MFFD's actual ingest cadence (likely 1ms TCP thermal trail → micro-batches), compression policy on chunks older than N days, continuous-aggregate candidates for the dashboard endpoints. | M | queued | Cite `aidocs/platform/87-timeseries-appid-migration.md` for the substrate model. |

| DB-OPT5 | **Frontend payload diet** — once query latency is honest, the next round of wins is on response-shape. ### BATCH-API — 2026-05-23 (bulk endpoints for metadata-heavy passes)

User directive 2026-05-23 after v16 deploy block landed: *"backlog batch API"*. v16's Pass 1 + Pass 2 issue tens of thousands of individual POST/PATCH calls (one per source DO) — the metadata work that's cheap individually but expensive in aggregate. v16's 3-pass design is mainly bottlenecked here, not at the per-DO file/TS/SD write level.

A batch API on the dest reduces N round-trips to N/B (B = batch size, e.g. 100). For an MFFD-scale ingest with ~30K source DOs this is the difference between 30K HTTP calls and 300 — likely **10-30× speedup on Pass 1 + Pass 2** combined.

| ID | Slice | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| BATCH-API-1 | **Design + spec** — endpoints under `/v2/` (the fork's development surface): `POST /v2/collections/{appId}/data-objects:batch` (bulk create, body = array of DataObjectIO with name/desc/attrs/parentAppId/predecessorAppIds, transactional or best-effort per `?mode=`); `PATCH /v2/collections/{appId}/data-objects:batch` (bulk update); same shape for `/v2/structured-data-containers/{appId}/payloads:batch` (bulk SD writes for tight ref groups). Body cap configurable (e.g. 1000 items / 10MB whichever smaller). Response: per-item `{index, id, appId, status, error?}`. | M | queued | OpenAPI spec lives in `backend/src/main/java/de/dlr/shepard/v2/.../resources/`. |
| BATCH-API-2 | **Backend implementation** — Quarkus REST resource + service. Transaction shape per `?mode=`: `mode=atomic` rollback on any failure; `mode=besteffort` partial success returns per-item status (default). Reuses existing OGM + persistence logic; just amortizes session+transaction cost across N items. Optimistic-locking for PATCH (revision check per item). Permission check applies per item. | L | queued | Pairs with existing `DataObjectService.create/update` — wraps in a `@Transactional` outer + per-item loop. |
| BATCH-API-3 | **Importer adoption** — v16.1 importer uses batch endpoints when available. Pass 1: chunk all_src into batches of 100, POST `:batch`; map src_do_id → dest_id from response array. Pass 2: chunk dest_id list into batches of 100, PATCH `:batch` with parentId + predecessorIds. Pass 3 (per-DO file/TS/SD writes) stays per-DO because payloads are heavy + benefit from worker fan-out rather than batching. | M | queued | Detect support via `OPTIONS /v2/.../data-objects:batch` or feature flag. Fall back to per-DO calls if endpoint absent (operators on older fork still work). |
| BATCH-API-4 | **Per-substrate batch primitives audit** — see if Mongo `bulkWrite`, PostgreSQL `INSERT INTO ... VALUES (...), (...), ...`, TimescaleDB `COPY`, Neo4j `UNWIND` are being used optimally underneath BATCH-API-2's per-item loop. Eke out the last 2-3× by collapsing the inner loop into a single substrate-native bulk op. | L | queued | Profile first; the easy 10× from "one HTTP request" is independent of this. |
| BATCH-API-5 | **Tests** — TestBatchEndpoint covering: atomic-mode rollback on item-3 failure, besteffort-mode partial-success accounting, permission filtering at item level (some items rejected, others succeed), 413 response when body exceeds cap. Importer-side: `tests/test_v16_batch.py` verifies the chunking + fallback path. | M | queued | |

**Acceptance**: re-running a 30K-DO MFFD import with BATCH-API in place completes Pass 1 + Pass 2 in <5 min (vs ~50 min today). Pass 3 unchanged (workers=4 worker bound stays the bottleneck for payload-heavy work).

### V16-PRESERVE-HIERARCHY — 2026-05-23 (replace v15's flat shape with full source-DO tree replication)

User directive 2026-05-23 after v15 hit steady-state ingest: *"so under one DO many DOs could be and then another... DOs to the bottom — along the way references ... is the script doing this"* + decision **B** when offered the trade-off. v15 flattens cube3's hierarchical DO tree (Step → Layer → Ply Group → Track) into a single step DO with thousands of refs whose names encode the source-DO identity. v16 ships the proper-fidelity design: replicate the source tree as actual dest DOs with parent/child + predecessor/successor edges + per-DO attributes.

**Fidelity gaps v15 has that v16 closes**:

- Source DO tree → flattened to single step DO (loses Layer / Ply Group / Track structure)
- Per-source-DO attributes → only step DO carries attrs (loses `layer_index`, `ply_orientation`, `track_idx`, `material_batch`, etc.)
- Per-source-DO predecessor/successor edges → not replicated (Track N→N+1 chain lost)
- Per-source-DO timestamps → only step DO carries import-time stamp

**What stays from v15**:

- Predefined SD containers (645000 + 645003) — these are SHARED across all leaf DOs of a step. Each leaf's structuredDataReference points at the shared container with its own oids list.
- TS container per step (e.g., 653673) — same shared-container pattern.
- File container per source DO — each source file lands as 1 file ref on the leaf dest DO that owned it in source.
- AUTH PROBE (v15.17), ENV-ALIAS (v15.17), uv-PEP-723 runner (v15.16), exit-0 break (v1.1), MFFD_SELFUPDATE / MFFD_CREATE_SEMANTIC_REPOS env opt-outs (v15.19) — all carry forward unchanged.

| ID | Slice | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| V16-IMPL-1 | **Recursive source traversal** — `iter_data_objects` extends to either (a) return all DOs incl. nested + script reconstructs tree via parentId, OR (b) recurse children explicitly. (a) is fewer cube3 round-trips; prefer it. Returned SourceDO must carry `parentId`, `childrenIds`, `predecessorIds`, `successorIds`, full `attributes`. | M | queued | Audit v5 `/collections/{c}/dataObjects` endpoint — does it return all-depth or top-level-only? If top-level: need `/dataObjects/{d}/children` traversal. |
| V16-IMPL-2 | **Dest tree creation** — for each source DO, create a dest DO whose parent is the dest-side mirror of the source's parent (step DO at the root). Two-pass: first pass creates all dest DOs without edges; second pass wires parent/child + predecessor/successor edges using a source-id → dest-id map. State file extends to map `src_do.do_id → dest_do_id` for resume safety. | L | queued | The two-pass is necessary because predecessor edges may forward-reference DOs not yet created. |
| V16-IMPL-3 | **Per-DO attribute copy** — copy ALL source DO attributes verbatim plus standard `source_*` markers (per v15.10). No attribute is privileged; every key the source carries lands on dest. Critical for `layer_index`, `ply_orientation`, etc. which are the queryable identity of each Track. | S | queued | Filter only operational shepard-internal attrs (`createdBy`, `appId`, etc. that the dest fills itself). |
| V16-IMPL-4 | **Reference placement at the correct depth** — file/TS/SD references land on the LEAF dest DO that carried the source ref, NOT on the step DO. Step DO becomes a pure parent container. State file granularity = per-source-DO-id × per-ref-kind × per-ref-id. | M | queued | The big behaviour change. v15's `dest_do_id = step_dest_do_id` becomes `dest_do_id = src_to_dest_map[src_do.do_id]`. |
| V16-IMPL-5 | **Resume safety** — state file's `do_done`/`file_done`/`ts_done`/`structured_done` keys all key by SOURCE DO ID (not name). `dest_id_map` persisted to state so a resumed run knows the dest-side mapping. Idempotent: re-running over a half-done state yields zero duplicate dest DOs. | M | queued | Critical — re-runs are the norm during ingest tuning. |
| V16-IMPL-6 | **Bridgewelding parallel paths** — source has multiple `Execution YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS` DOs under Bridgewelding, plus `Process Data N`, `AF_9` etc. These are sibling at the same depth (children of Bridgewelding step). v16 preserves them all as sibling dest DOs. | S | queued | Reference 50-ref listing seen during today's debug shows the shape. |
| V16-IMPL-7 | **Test fixtures + unit tests** — recursion correctness, two-pass edge wiring, resume safety, dest_id_map persistence. `tests/test_v16_hierarchy.py`. | M | queued | Before live deploy. |
| V16-IMPL-8 | **Deploy + re-run** — wipe dest MFFD-Dropbox 652941 (already wiped per this row's prompt), launch v16 from clean state. ETA roughly same as v15 (cube3 source-pull is the bottleneck, not the dest writes). | S | blocked-on-1..7 | Cube redeploy + tmux launch using existing runbook. |

**Acceptance**: at completion, MFFD-Dropbox contains a tree of dest DOs matching cube3's source tree — step DOs at the root, Layer / Ply Group / Track / Execution DOs nested below, leaf-DO references attached at the correct depth, predecessor/successor edges between sibling DOs preserved. UI shows the AFP digital thread structurally, not just as a flat ref-list.

### MFFD-GRAPH-PRUNE — 2026-05-23 (post-ingest graph hygiene)

User directive 2026-05-23 mid-MFFD-redeploy: *"backlog maybe prune graph afterwards"*. After MFFD ingest drains, run a graph-pruning pass to remove the artifacts accumulated during today's bug-chase (orphan TS containers 528098 / 589657 / 599903, the 52 `tapelaying/Track N (Run M)/Timeseries` Neo4j shadow nodes with NULL `id`, any DataObjects that ended up with broken `:HAS_REFERENCE` edges to deleted containers, and the legacy SD containers that survived the wipes). Pre-mutation snapshot per `PRE-MUT-SNAP` before any destructive Cypher.

| ID | Slice | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| MFFD-PRUNE-1 | **Inventory the graph debris** — Cypher queries that produce an honest count: orphan `:TimeseriesContainer` (no `:USES_CONTAINER` back-edge), shadow `:TimeseriesContainer` with NULL `c.id`, `:StructuredDataContainer` not in the predefined set (`645000`/`645003`), `:DataObject` with refs pointing at non-existent containers, `:FileReference` orphan blobs in Garage. Output: `aidocs/agent-findings/mffd-graph-debris-<date>.md`. | S | queued | First pass — no deletes. Just counts + sample rows. |
| MFFD-PRUNE-2 | **Snapshot before deletion** — per `PRE-MUT-SNAP` rule, snapshot the scope `(c:TimeseriesContainer WHERE …) + (c:StructuredDataContainer WHERE …) + (do:DataObject WHERE c.id IS NULL)` to `snapshots-system` collection with PROV-O attribution. | S | queued | Blocks PRUNE-3 until snapshot artefact verified. |
| MFFD-PRUNE-3 | **Execute prune** — Cypher: `MATCH (c:TimeseriesContainer) WHERE c.id IS NULL OR NOT (c)<-[:USES_CONTAINER]-(:TimeseriesReference) DETACH DELETE c;` and equivalents for SD-side debris. Honor the integrity rule (`feedback_referenced_data_infinite_retention.md`) — anything with active refs stays. | M | queued | Closes the loop on today's bug-chase. |
| MFFD-PRUNE-4 | **TimescaleDB chunk cleanup** — for the TS containers we pruned in Neo4j, the underlying TimescaleDB rows are still there (the REST DELETE blocks per TSDB-DELETE-LIMIT). Direct `SELECT drop_chunks('timeseries_data_points', …)` scoped to the dead container_ids. | S | queued | Pairs with TSDB-DDL-1 / TSDB-DDL-2 once they ship. |

### TSDB-DELETE-LIMIT — 2026-05-23 (TimescaleDB DML decompression limit blocks TS container delete)

Surfaced during the MFFD-tapelaying triage (2026-05-23 ~13:36 UTC). `DELETE /shepard/api/timeseriesContainers/{id}` returns HTTP 500 for any TS container whose FK-cascade chain touches >100K rows in compressed chunks. The backend code is innocent — TimescaleDB substrate config knob `timescaledb.max_tuples_decompressed_per_dml_transaction = 100000` (default) is the gate.

Stacktrace from backend log (ref `10295074-4c77-4319-92c7-406efac48288`):
```
JDBC exception executing SQL [ERROR: tuple decompression limit exceeded by operation
  Detail: current limit: 100000, tuples decompressed: 3487063
  Hint: Consider increasing timescaledb.max_tuples_decompressed_per_dml_transaction or set to 0 (unlimited).
  Where: SQL statement "DELETE FROM ONLY \"_timescaledb_internal\".\"_hyper_1_38_chunk\" WHERE $1 OPERATOR(pg_catalog.=) \"timeseries_id\""]
[delete from timeseries te1_0 where te1_0.container_id=?]
```

| ID | Slice | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| TSDB-DDL-1 | **Raise the decompression limit in the TimescaleDB container env.** Three placement options: (a) `ALTER SYSTEM SET timescaledb.max_tuples_decompressed_per_dml_transaction = 0` baked into a migration; (b) `command:` arg on the `timescaledb` service in `infrastructure/docker-compose.yml` (`-c timescaledb.max_tuples_decompressed_per_dml_transaction=0`); (c) `SET timescaledb.max_tuples_decompressed_per_dml_transaction = 0` per-session in the Hibernate / JDBC connection-pool initializer. Recommendation: **(b)** — declarative, visible to operators in compose. `0` = unlimited; safe because Shepard's typical delete is admin-initiated. | S | queued | Pairs with `feedback_db_audit_includes_stack.md` (compose env / driver knobs are in scope for DB-audit). Sister issue: explicit FK cascade trigger could be replaced by `drop_chunks()` for whole-container deletes — see TSDB-DDL-2. |
| TSDB-DDL-2 | **Chunk-aware container delete path** — for `DELETE /timeseriesContainers/{id}`, the right substrate primitive is `SELECT drop_chunks('timeseries_data_points', older_than => now())` scoped to `timeseries_id IN (SELECT id FROM timeseries WHERE container_id = ?)`, NOT row-by-row DELETE. Drops compressed chunks without decompression. Order-of-magnitude faster + bypasses the decompression-limit issue entirely. Replace the JPA cascade for whole-container TS deletes. | M | queued | This is the structural fix. TSDB-DDL-1 is the immediate unblock. |
| TSDB-DDL-3 | **Apply retroactively: today's TS-tapelaying consolidation** — once TSDB-DDL-1 ships, the deferred 589657 + 599903 delete (528098 is strict superset, zero data loss) should succeed via the existing REST DELETE endpoint. Acceptance test for TSDB-DDL-1. | S | queued | Cross-references PRE-MUT-SNAP5 (which would gate this through a snapshot pair when that mechanism ships). |

### PRE-MUT-SNAP — 2026-05-23 (pre-mutation snapshot mechanism — gate on every cleanup / purge / migration)

User directive 2026-05-23, during the MFFD TS-tapelaying-duplicate triage: *"thats why we need provenance .. and snapshots on mutations"*. The trigger was a sloppy "duplicate-looking" call on 3 TS containers (528098/589657/599903) where a row-level spot-check turned out to be required to confirm safe-to-delete; the REST DELETE 500'd before any harm was done, but the **structural fix is to gate every mutation behind a snapshot pair**, not rely on backend failure as the safety net.

Builds on `project_snapshot_boundaries.md` (existing memory: "every larger transformation gets a snapshot pair") + `feedback_referenced_data_infinite_retention.md` (referenced data has infinite retention; only orphans are deletion-eligible) — this section ships the mechanism so those rules are enforced, not just documented.

| ID | Slice | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| PRE-MUT-SNAP1 | **Pre-mutation snapshot contract** — design doc `aidocs/ops/<NN>-pre-mutation-snapshots.md`. Defines: every mutation pathway (cleanup / purge / migration / storage rebalance / FS1e move / SM1 orphan-collect) MUST take a pre-mutation snapshot of the affected scope BEFORE the first destructive operation. Scope = the substrate slice that would be mutated (e.g. `timeseries_data_points WHERE container_id IN (...)` + the corresponding Neo4j subgraph + Mongo collections + Garage objects). Snapshot artefact = a `:Snapshot` DataObject in a dedicated `snapshots-system` collection with PROV-O attribution of WHO triggered it + WHAT it covers + the artefact hash. Snapshots are retained for a configurable grace window (default: 90 days). | M | queued | Companion to `project_snapshot_boundaries.md`. Cite `feedback_referenced_data_infinite_retention.md` as the kill-switch criterion. |
| PRE-MUT-SNAP2 | **Substrate-native snapshot primitives** — implement the per-substrate snapshot operations the contract requires. TimescaleDB: `INSERT INTO snapshots.<table>_snap SELECT * FROM <table> WHERE <scope>`. Neo4j: `apoc.export.cypher.query(scope-cypher, file, {format:'plain'})` to a snapshot artefact. Mongo: `db.<coll>.aggregate([{$match: scope}, {$out: 'snapshots.<coll>_<session>'}])`. Garage: `garage bucket snapshot` (if available) or `garage block download` + tar. Each primitive returns a `SnapshotResult{substrate, scope, rowCount, sizeBytes, artefactUri, sha256, durationMs}`. | M | queued | Lives in backend (Java) `de.dlr.shepard.ops.SnapshotService` + a Quarkus REST surface `POST /v2/admin/snapshots`. |
| PRE-MUT-SNAP3 | **Gate every mutation pathway** — wire SnapshotService into every existing cleanup / migration / purge entry point: the orphan-wipe scripts under `examples/mffd-showcase/scripts/`, the SM1 `purgeOrphans` operation (task #74), the FS1e migration runner, the `mffd-completeness-check.py` consolidation suggestion (when it gets that), and the `shepard-admin <feature> set-*` commands that touch data. Gate behaviour: `--no-snapshot` flag REQUIRED to skip; default = take snapshot, refuse to proceed if snapshot fails. | L | queued | Touches ≥5 entry points. Land incrementally per pathway — don't block ship of the mechanism on full coverage. |
| PRE-MUT-SNAP4 | **Rollback runbook** — `docs/admin/runbooks/rollback-from-snapshot.md`. Single-page operator procedure: given a snapshot id, restore the affected scope. Per the `feedback_admin_runbooks_pattern.md` contract: numbered steps, host indicator per step, expected stdout, end-state verification (a fresh `SELECT COUNT(*)` matching the pre-snapshot count). Includes the cross-substrate restore order (Neo4j → TimescaleDB → Mongo → Garage) so referential integrity holds. | M | queued | Pairs with `feedback_admin_runbooks_pattern.md` (runbook contract) + `ADMIN-RUNBOOKS-LIBRARY` (the systematic library this row contributes to). |
| PRE-MUT-SNAP5 | **Apply retroactively: today's TS-tapelaying triage** — once the mechanism ships, the deferred MFFD-tapelaying consolidation (528098 keep, 589657 + 599903 delete) goes through the new path: snapshot first, then DELETE. Closes the loop on the situation that motivated the row. | S | queued | This is the **acceptance test**: if PRE-MUT-SNAP1..4 are right, this consolidation should be a two-line operator script. |

### DB — 2026-05-22 (database inventory + best-practices + anti-pattern hunt)

User directive 2026-05-22: *"database inverntiry best pracices review, antipattern avaidance on backlog"*. Survey the full multi-substrate landscape (Neo4j + Postgres + TimescaleDB + MongoDB + PostGIS + Garage S3) and codify what's good, what's drifting, and what's actively anti-pattern. Per `feedback_db_review_all_stores.md` — never single out one substrate.

| ID | Slice | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| DB-INV1 | **Inventory pass** — every Cypher migration (`V##__*.cypher`), every Flyway SQL migration (`db/migration/V*.sql`), every Mongo collection seed, every PostGIS geometry table, every Garage bucket. Output: `aidocs/data/<NN>-db-inventory.md` listing schema name + owner module + indices + active write-paths. | M | queued | Snapshot in time; refresh annually. Cross-references CLAUDE.md "always ship migrations idempotent + fail-fast". |
| DB-BP1 | **Best-practices catalogue** — what the fork does right per store. Examples: parametrised Cypher (post-C5/C5b shipped), JPA `@Entity` + Panache repository pattern (importer plugin), PostGIS index-on-create, Mongo collection naming convention. Each entry cites a representative commit. Output: `aidocs/data/<NN>-db-best-practices.md`. | M | queued | Living catalogue. Authors of new code copy from here. |
| DB-AP1 | **Anti-pattern hunt** — find every site that violates a known good practice. Candidates: string-concat'd Cypher (C5/C5b killed them but regressions grow back), N+1 query patterns (Neo4j AND Postgres), missing indices on hot-path foreign keys, GridFS used for files when Garage S3 is active, missing `ON DELETE CASCADE` on Postgres FKs where the parent is mutable, missing constraints on `:HasAppId` Neo4j labels, Mongo collections without TTL where the data is ephemeral. Output: `aidocs/agent-findings/db-antipatterns.md` listing every flagged site with severity (CRITICAL/MAJOR/MINOR) and remediation. | L | queued | Dispatched as multi-agent fan-out (one agent per substrate). Per `feedback_db_review_all_stores.md` MUST cover all six substrates. |
| DB-AP2 | **Cross-cutting findings** — patterns that span substrates. E.g. dual-source-of-truth (same field written to Neo4j AND Postgres), substrate-mismatch (timeseries lives in Timescale but the Neo4j `:Timeseries` label still carries denormalised metadata that can drift), schema-evolution gaps (migration added the field but the IO class doesn't surface it). Highest-value findings per SSOT discipline (`feedback_shacl_single_source_of_truth.md`). | M | queued | DB-AP1 enables DB-AP2 — run AP1 first per substrate, then AP2 reads the union. |
| DB-DOC1 | Roll the catalogues into operator-facing docs: `docs/reference/database-overview.md` (one-screen "what data lives where") + `docs/help/troubleshooting-databases.md` (operator-readable common issues + fixes). | S | queued | Last step. Surfaces the inventory to the Pages site. |

### TRACE — 2026-05-22 (requirements traceability)

| ID | Slice | Size | Status | Notes |

### P1 — 2026-05-16 (parallel DB connectivity)

| ID | Slice | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|
| P1 | Parallel startup DB warm + parallel recovery | done | New `DbConnectivityWarmer` (`@ApplicationScoped`, `@Observes StartupEvent`) fires one `Thread.ofVirtual()` per required `DbPinger` in parallel — total startup wait is now `max(latencies)` not `sum(latencies)`. Bounded by `shepard.migrations.connection-wait-timeout` (reused from `MigrationsRunner`; no new config key). `DbRecoveryScheduler.attemptRecovery()` now collects stale pingers then probes each in its own virtual thread (`CompletableFuture.allOf` blocks the tick). Both use `RequestContextController.activate/deactivate` per thread so JPA `EntityManager` injections in `TimescalePinger` / `PostGisPinger` work correctly off the caller thread. Per-DB `DbHealthState` independently tracks each outcome. 7 new unit tests in `DbConnectivityWarmerTest` (including timing proof: 3 × 300 ms pingers finish in < 950 ms wall-clock); 2 new tests added to `DbRecoverySchedulerTest`. |

### VIS — 2026-05-22 (visualization plugin family)

Survey: `aidocs/agent-findings/vis-plugin-survey.md`. Broadens the Trace3D seed
(`aidocs/agent-findings/trace3d-spike.md`, task #142) into a coherent plugin
family covering 3D paths/traces, vector fields/CFD, voxel/volumetric (REM/EM/μCT),
and surface meshes. **Extended 2026-05-22** with categories 5 (CAD data) and
6 (FEM result files) per
`aidocs/agent-findings/vis-plugin-survey-addendum-cad-fem.md` —
7 categories total, 5 plugins + 2 sidecars. All rows queued; pick-up order:
VIS-S1 → VIS-T1 → VIS-V1 → VIS-X1 → **VIS-C1 → VIS-F1** → VIS-S2 → VIS-S3
(stretch).

**Critical context for VIS-T1:** `@tresjs/nuxt` repo was archived Feb 1, 2026.
`@tresjs/core` itself (v5.8.1, May 2026) is still actively maintained. Use core
directly via an in-plugin `useTres()` composable; do NOT depend on the archived
Nuxt module. This is a correction to `aidocs/agent-findings/trace3d-spike.md`
which assumed `@tresjs/nuxt` was available — see survey §1.2 for the rationale.

Vendor-isolation pattern is Shepard's structural answer to a gap most competing RDM platforms punt on entirely (Kadi4Mat / SciCat typically ship no FEM viewer). `cadOverlay` slot composes vis-cad's resolved glTF into the same `<VtkScene>` — MFFD's "as-designed vs as-deformed" comparison case. ### M4I — 2026-05-23 (metadata4ing deepening)

User directive 2026-05-23: *"how to deepen metadata4ing (m4i) integration"*.
Design lands at `aidocs/semantics/94-metadata4ing-integration-design.md`.
**Critical finding** surfaced during research: the current
`ProvJsonLdRenderer` emits **non-canonical predicates**
(`m4i:hasMethod` / `m4i:hasInput` / `m4i:hasOutput`) that do
not exist in canonical m4i 1.4.0 — see M4I-b. Latest m4i
version is **1.4.0 (2025-12-08)**; the shipped bundle pins it
already, no version bump needed.

| ID | Slice | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| M4I-a | Promote `metadata4ing.ttl` stub → fetch canonical TTL on first seed via existing `canonicalUrl` + `fetchOnSeed` flag (NASA Thesaurus N1e pattern). Stub stays in JAR as offline fallback. Acceptance: ≥ 100 m4i `:Resource` rows in n10s after fresh start. | S (1 d) | queued | `aidocs/semantics/94 §4.1`. Builds on `aidocs/44 §7a` N1e precedent + `aidocs/semantics/65 §2.3` canonical-URL pattern. No backend Java churn beyond a flag flip on the manifest entry. |
| M4I-b | **CRITICAL bug-shaped fix.** Rewrite m4i branch of `ProvJsonLdRenderer.render(...)` to emit canonical predicates: `m4i:hasMethod` → **`m4i:realizesMethod`**; `m4i:hasInput` → **`obo:RO_0002233`** (OBO Relations Ontology, already preseeded via ONT1a); `m4i:hasOutput` → **`obo:RO_0002234`**. Extend `@context` with `"obo"` prefix when profile=m4i. Add `m4i:investigates` from activity to investigated entity on read actions. | S (1 d) | queued | `aidocs/semantics/94 §4.2`. Verified against canonical OWL at `https://nfdi4ing.pages.rwth-aachen.de/metadata4ing/metadata4ing/` on 2026-05-23. Add SHACL self-test asserting canonical predicates. AWARE in `aidocs/34` flagged BREAKING for any m4i consumer that depended on the old non-canonical names (low real-world risk; no known consumer; discipline is the point). |
| M4I-c | `m4i:DataObjectShape` SHACL contract + `M4iDataObjectRenderer` + content-neg `Accept: application/ld+json; profile=metadata4ing` on `GET /v2/data-objects/{appId}` (mirrors PROV1h on `/v2/provenance/*`). Mandatory triples: `m4i:InvestigatedObject` type, `dcterms:identifier`, `dcterms:title`, `schema:dateCreated`. Optional: `m4i:hasIdentifier` (KIP1a PID), `obo:RO_0002233/4` (predecessor / successor), `prov:wasGeneratedBy` (most-recent Activity), `m4i:realizesMethod` (when actionKind known), `schema:keywords` (annotations). Refactor UH1b renderer to consume same shape. | M (3–4 d) | queued | `aidocs/semantics/94 §4.3`. Depends on M4I-a + M4I-b. Conceptually slots under `aidocs/semantics/95` SHACL substrate; ships before full substrate by reading the shape file at startup the same way ontology bundles do. Acceptance: pyShacl validation passes on every DataObject in MFFD + LUMEN seed Collections. |
| M4I-d | Promote `:Activity.actionKind` / instruments / annotations to first-class m4i individuals. Three sub-slices: **(d-1)** mint stable `shepard:method/<kind>` IRIs typed `m4i:Method` on first use; **(d-2)** mint `shepard:tool/<typename>` IRIs typed `m4i:Tool`, link via `m4i:hasEmployedTool`; **(d-3)** annotation keys matching SHACL `m4i:hasNumericalVariable` slot render as typed `m4i:NumericalVariable` blank nodes with QUDT unit refs. | M (3 d) | queued | `aidocs/semantics/94 §4.4`. Depends on M4I-c (shape contract for what counts as a numeric variable). Acceptance: SPARQL `?step m4i:realizesMethod ?m. ?m a m4i:Method.` returns ≥ 1 row over MFFD seed. Read-time computation (lazy promotion) — no write-throughput hit. |
| M4I-e | Operator runbook `docs/reference/nfdi4ing-federation.md` + companion task page `docs/help/register-with-nfdi4ing.md`. Walk through: m4i bundle enable verification → Terminology Service self-registration → Unhide harvester pointing → (forward-looking) NFDI4Ing Archetype Doris registration for HPMC use cases. Pure docs, no code. | S (1 d) | queued | `aidocs/semantics/94 §4.5`. Pairs with `aidocs/integrations/67 §7`. Acceptance: real ZLP Augsburg / Lampoldshausen operator can follow it end-to-end in ≤ 30 min. |
| M4I-f | Add `metadata4ing-hpmc` bundle to preseed manifest — m4i HPMC sub-ontology for high-performance measurement + computing workflows. SHA-256-pinned TTL stub + canonical URL + `required=false`, default-on. Stub covers headline classes (`m4i:HpmcWorkflow` etc.); N1c admin refresh pulls full canonical OWL. | S (1 d) | queued | `aidocs/semantics/94 §4.6`. Source: <https://nfdi4ing.de/5-23-2/>. Targeted (HPMC-using operators only — LUMEN hot-fire DAQ, MFFD AFP telemetry). Parallel to M4I-a. Document transitive dependencies (potentially NFDI-MatWerk / MaRDI terms) in the bundle's manifest entry. |

Recommended landing order (per `aidocs/semantics/94 §9`):
**M4I-a → M4I-b → M4I-c → M4I-e → M4I-d → M4I-f**. Total ~10–11 days.
M4I-b lands first regardless of slice ordering — correctness, not deepening.

### SWEEP — 2026-05-23 (deferred items surfaced from repo grep)

Sweep result from a cross-cutting `grep -E 'TODO|FIXME|deferred|follow-up|out of scope|queued'` pass across `backend/`, `frontend/`, `plugins/`, `examples/`, `docs/`, `aidocs/agent-findings/`, `aidocs/{platform,integrations,ops,semantics,strategy,ux,workflows,reference}/*.md`, `.github/workflows/`, `Makefile`, and `backend/pom.xml`. 320 existing row IDs were extracted from this file and used as a dedup filter — every row below is **not** already on the backlog. Full inventory + source citations: `aidocs/agent-findings/repo-task-sweep-2026-05-23.md`.

Rationale: per `feedback_backlog_for_later.md` ("things-for-later go on a maintained backlog, not in prose docs") and `feedback_backlog_consult_context.md` (every row cites its source). The risk being closed is the slow rot where a `TODO(IMP1)` in `ImportV2Rest.java` or a "this is a follow-up" footnote in a design doc never becomes a row, and the deferral is forgotten.

Skew: 5 CRITICAL, 49 MAJOR, 17 MINOR, 14 NICE-to-have. Highest-priority item to ship: **`MFG5`** — enforce DataObject `status` as a closed enum at the persistence boundary. Quoting `aidocs/agent-findings/manufacturing-quality.md §11.2`: *"the single largest gap between Shepard's current design and aerospace quality record requirements"* — one backend PR, no migration on shipped data beyond a value-set check.

| MFFD-IMPORT-PERF1 | **Real worker fan-out for `run_source_mode_workers`.** Extract the per-DO loop body (`mffd-import-v15.py` L2495..2598) into a callable `_process_one_source_do(...)` and submit one future per source DO. Bound at 4 concurrent cube3 GETs + 4 dest POSTs per `aidocs/93 §5`. Today the wrapper is a fake fan-out — it spawns the pool, runs `lambda: True` probes, then calls `run_source_mode` SEQUENTIALLY (`mffd-import-v15.py` L2983..2999). `--workers N` does nothing for throughput. | M | **done (v15.8)** | MAJOR | `aidocs/agent-findings/mffd-import-slowness-diagnose-2026-05-23.md §5 Hypothesis #1` | Shipped 2026-05-23 in v15.8 (manifest published to FileContainer 473932). Per-DO body extracted into `_process_one_source_do(src_do, do_bar)` closure inside `run_source_mode`. Driver submits one future per source DO via `ThreadPoolExecutor(max_workers=workers)` with `as_completed`-based drain + refill keeping the pool saturated. `tqdm.update(1)` happens only in the driver thread. `ImportState` gains `_lock: RLock` covering all read+write ops. `existing_names` hoisted to per-step snapshot (no N parallel calls for the same dest list). `run_source_mode_workers` simplified to a thin forwarder; tests in `tests/test_worker_pool.py` updated. |
| MFFD-IMPORT-PERF2 | **Lazy enrichment in `iter_data_objects`.** Yield a stub `SourceDO(do_id, name, attrs, ...)` with `file_refs=None / ts_refs=None / sd_refs=None`; fetch refs only when the per-DO `state.is_*_done` skip check would not fire. Today (`mffd-import-v15.py` L707..711) the script fires 3 cube3 GETs per source DO BEFORE the L2504/L2541/L2570 state-skip checks. On a fully-resumed run that's 25 371 wasted WAN round-trips for an 8 457-DO collection. | S | **done (v15.8)** | MAJOR | `aidocs/agent-findings/mffd-import-slowness-diagnose-2026-05-23.md §5 Hypothesis #2` | Shipped 2026-05-23 in v15.8 (manifest published to FileContainer 473932). `SourceDO.file_refs / ts_refs / structured_refs` now default to `None`; `iter_data_objects` yields stubs (no enrichment GETs). New `ShepardClient._load_file_refs / _load_ts_refs / _load_structured_refs` helpers fetch + cache on first access via `SourceDO._src_coll_id`. Per-DO loop body calls these AFTER per-ref state-skip would short-circuit. Fully-done DO on resume: 0 cube3 GETs (was 3). |
| MFFD-IMPORT-PERF3 | **Preempt-friendly self-update apply.** After each completed source DO, check `if updater.update_event.is_set(): break` so the script gracefully exits to the `finally`-block self-update path (`mffd-import-v15.py` L4154..4157). Today the updater detects v15.7 at 60-s cadence (137 events) but the apply is gated by `run_source_mode` returning — operator sees "stuck on 15.6" for 2 h 17 min while the loop runs. Observability win, not a throughput win. | XS | queued | MINOR | `aidocs/agent-findings/mffd-import-slowness-diagnose-2026-05-23.md §5 Hypothesis #3` | 10 lines after L2598. Pair with the dest-side `gauge_cube3_inflight_requests` metric (MFFD-IMPORT-PERF4 below). |
| MFFD-IMPORT-PERF4 | **Add `gauge_cube3_inflight_requests` + `gauge_cube3_p95_latency_ms` to the `Telemetry` class.** Today the operator's only signal that the script is "alive" is heartbeat cadence + `counter_dos_processed`. ### GH-INFRA — 2026-05-23 (GitHub features integration)

Full survey: `aidocs/strategy/83-github-features-leverage.md`. The
guiding rule (also pinned in `feedback_github_features.md`): default is
"don't add a new GitHub feature unless solo-dev cost is near zero AND
external-contributor / security-posture value is high"; `aidocs/16`
stays SSOT — Issues are NOT a backlog mirror.

Decision matrix per feature lives in the survey doc above.

| ID | Slice | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| GH-INFRA1 | Templates + CODEOWNERS + Dependabot + canonical labels + release-notes scaffolding + PR template mirroring CLAUDE.md "Always:" rules + CONTRIBUTING.md "Filing issues" / "PR discipline" sections + the survey doc + this row. Pure config-as-code; no API calls; no live changes to the GitHub repo until merged + the operator actions below are taken. | M | done | Shipped 2026-05-23 on the worktree branch in one commit. Files: `.github/release.yml`, `.github/workflows/release-notes.yml`, `.github/workflows/sync-labels.yml`, `.github/ISSUE_TEMPLATE/{config,bug-report,feature-request,docs-improvement,security-finding}.yml`, `.github/pull_request_template.md`, `.github/CODEOWNERS`, `.github/dependabot.yml`, `.github/labels.yml`, `docs/ops/cut-a-release.md`, `docs/ops/github-projects-board-setup.md`, `aidocs/strategy/83-github-features-leverage.md`, CONTRIBUTING.md additions. |
