### GH-PM — 2026-05-23 (GitHub project-management policies)

Full policy: `aidocs/strategy/85-github-project-management-policies.md`.
The shape: `aidocs/16` is the SSOT backlog; GitHub Issues are the narrow
4-gate subset (external-pickup / security / repro-bug / agent in-flight);
sync direction is one-way (aidocs/16 → Issue); the unified state machine
maps doc front-matter ↔ aidocs/16 Status ↔ GH `status:*` / `stage:*`
labels ↔ Projects v2 columns byte-for-byte (see `aidocs/00-doc-stages.md`).
Releases cut on coherent-feature-set boundary with the §5 pre-flight
checklist. The end-state test is `scripts/trace-feature.sh <ID>` — nine
surfaces resolved per feature.

| ID | Slice | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| GH-PM1 | The policy doc itself + `scripts/trace-feature.sh` helper + CLAUDE.md "Always: file Issues + cut releases per `aidocs/strategy/85`" amendment + this aidocs/16 section + the `feedback_github_pm_policies.md` memory rule. Sets out the unified state machine, the 4-gate Issues filter, branch + commit + PR + milestone + release + label conventions, the §14 traceability query, and the §15 anti-patterns. | S | done | Shipped 2026-05-23 on the worktree branch in one commit. Files: `aidocs/strategy/85-github-project-management-policies.md`, `scripts/trace-feature.sh`, `CLAUDE.md` (one new "Always:" section), `aidocs/16-dispatcher-backlog.md` (this section), `/root/.claude/projects/-opt-shepard/memory/feedback_github_pm_policies.md`, MEMORY.md index entry. Validated end-to-end against `FS1b` — all nine surfaces resolved. |
| GH-PM2 | Wire `scripts/build-traceability-index.py` (TRACE-A) into `.github/workflows/pages.yml` so the rendered `docs/reference/traceability.md` updates on every push to `main` and ships on the GitHub Pages site. Operator-visible traceability — anyone can answer "what shipped under FS1b?" from a public URL. | S | queued | Gated on TRACE-A landing on `main` + `.github/workflows/pages.yml` being audit-trail-ready. Single-file workflow edit + one `python3` invocation. |
| GH-PM3 | Pre-commit hook (`.git/hooks/commit-msg` template under `scripts/hooks/`) that validates PR / commit message titles against the Conventional-Commits + aidocs/16 row-ID convention from §7. Rejects `feat(fs1b): …` (lowercase ID), `feat(FS1B): …` (wrong case), `feat: …` (no scope), and `feat(unknown-id): …` (ID not in aidocs/16). Opt-in (operator runs `make install-hooks`); recommended via CONTRIBUTING.md. | M | queued | After GH-PM2. The strict-uppercase rule is in §7 anti-pattern #4; the hook turns the soft rule into a hard gate locally before CI catches it. |
| GH-PM4 | Nightly drift check: cron-driven `gh issue list --search "in:title <ID-pattern>"` ↔ `aidocs/16` status diff. Pure read-only; produces a daily report in `aidocs/agent-findings/issue-drift-<date>.md`. Gated on **external-contribution velocity** picking up (same gate as GH-INFRA4) — at solo-dev cadence the drift surface is empty and the cron noise isn't worth it. | M | blocked | Blocking condition: external-contributor velocity threshold not yet met. Re-evaluate quarterly alongside GH-INFRA4. |
| FOCUS-2026-05-23-2 | **Pages page: "Advisory board" — the 10 personas summarised as the project's standing AI-driven expert board.** One card per persona (Strategy Aligner, API Scrutinizer, RDM, IME/AQE, Ontologist, Ecosystem Advocate, AI Specialist, Reluctant Senior, Digital Native, Core Tech/UX). | FOCUS-2026-05-23-1 | **Backfill other project features in the same pattern as GH-PM5.** When the GH-PM5 backfill lands, the pattern (synthetic-but-transparent + captured-as-Shepard-dataset) generalises. Candidates: (a) persona findings on past designs (backfill personas reviewing already-shipped code, each with transparency marker); (b) bibliography entries for past commits where a cited source applies; (c) `:Activity` PROV-O rows reconstructed from git log; (d) release notes for shipped-but-untagged work pre-v6.0.0-rc.1; (e) backfilled snapshots on past collection states (G1 backfill on existing collections). Creates a Collection `gh-pm-backfill-synthetic-2026-05-23` on `shepard-api.nuclide.systems` with `synthetic_batch=true`, one DataObject per filed Issue + per Milestone, predecessor links to source aidocs/16 rows, `fair2r:modeOfProduction "ai"` + `fair2r:syntheticBackfill true` annotations on every DataObject, pointer to the generation-rule plan doc. | GH-PM5 | **Backfill from `aidocs/16` ↔ Issues + Milestones + Releases on policy adoption, with mandatory per-artefact TRANSPARENCY MARKER.** Every backfilled Issue body opens with `🤖 **BACKFILL** — created retroactively YYYY-MM-DD as part of GH-PM5 adoption. Original work: commit <hash>, date <date>. Audit trail: <aidocs row + persona findings>.` Every Milestone description carries the BACKFILL marker. Persona findings backfilled review the SHIPPED artefact only; never claim retroactive prescience. Per `feedback_no_synthetic_provenance.md` in agent memory. | M | **done** | Executed 2026-05-23 alongside the §85 stage-flip. Backfill plan + execution log at `aidocs/agent-findings/gh-pm-backfill-plan-2026-05-23.md`. Milestones created: `v6.0.0-rc.1`, `v6.0.0-rc.2`, `v6.0.0`, `v6.x — backlog (no milestone yet)` — first three carry BACKFILL marker on their description. Per-Issue body opens with BACKFILL marker per §85 §8.1. Operator approval gate replaced by **artefact-level transparency-marker discipline** — the synthetic nature is disclosed in the artefact itself per `feedback_no_synthetic_provenance.md` refinement. ### OBS — 2026-05-23 (recursive self-observability)

The principle is documented in `feedback_shepard_measures_itself.md`:
Shepard's own ingest-rate metrics live INSIDE Shepard's TimeseriesContainer
substrate, not in a parallel observability stack. The MFFD-Dropbox import
session was the first concrete instance — the chart updates by the same
TS chart UI a researcher already uses.

| ID | Slice | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| OBS-MFFD1 | `scripts/mffd-import-stats-collector.py` polls `/v2/collections/{appId}/data-objects` every 5 min, walks per-DO refs for file/TS/SD counters, runs `docker exec shepard-garage /garage bucket info shepard-files` for the object-store size, and POSTs 11 channels per tick to `TimeseriesContainer` 590324 linked to `DataObject` 590344 in the MFFD-Dropbox collection. Bootstrap is idempotent; the `TimeseriesReference` is lazily created after the first tick materialises channels (the v5 `Bug A` minItems:1 constraint, learned from v15.2). Ships a systemd timer pair (`infrastructure/systemd/mffd-import-stats-collector.{service,timer}`) so operators can replace the ad-hoc background process. Plottable via the existing TS chart UI — no new frontend code. | S | done | Shipped 2026-05-23 (this commit). Files: `scripts/mffd-import-stats-collector.py`, `infrastructure/systemd/mffd-import-stats-collector.{service,timer}`, `docs/help/observing-an-import.md`, this row, `aidocs/data/00-model-inventory.md §8` row, `feedback_shepard_measures_itself.md`. Verified: first tick at 23:07:24Z wrote 11/11 channels (`DO=8, files=0, garage=160300 B`); second tick at 23:08:19Z saw `TSrefs=1, channels=11` confirming the lazy reference creation. |
| OBS-MFFD2 | Generalise the collector to ANY import job: lift the MFFD-specific name-pattern table into a per-collection config + accept any collection-appId. Land as `scripts/import-stats-collector.py` (drop the `mffd-` prefix) plus an admin UI for picking which collections to instrument. | M | queued | Promotes the recursive-observability pattern to a first-class tool. Pairs with the `OBS-MFFD3` admin dashboard. |
| OBS-MFFD3 | Dashboard view summarising all in-flight imports: list every `ImportStats-*` DataObject across all collections + a `dos_total` sparkline + a delta-since-last-tick. Plugs into the existing Collections list or lands as `/v2/admin/imports`. | M | queued | "What's actually being ingested right now?" admin view. Dep on `OBS-MFFD2`. Pairs with the `GH-INFRA3` release gate. |

| WIZARD-JSON-INTERPRETABLE | **Process wizards emit a JSON manifest of every action taken.** User-flagged 2026-05-23 *"make process wizards jason interpretable - whatever that means"*. Today's UI wizards (Create-from-template, ImportManifest helper, AnomalyDetection setup, future spatial-region annotator) capture user intent in form-state, translate it into REST writes (POST Collection / POST DataObject / POST Annotation / link refs / set attrs), and produce no durable per-action record other than the resulting Shepard entities + the PROV1a `:Activity` audit trail. The gap: an external agent (Claude / MCP / another Shepard instance / a downstream automation) can't re-read what the wizard *intended* — only what it *produced*. **Spec:** every wizard run emits a `wizard-run.json` artifact attached to the resulting top-level entity as a FileReference (`name="wizard-manifest.json"`, attribute `kind:wizard-manifest`). Manifest shape: `{wizard_id, wizard_version, user, started_at, finished_at, form_inputs: {...verbatim form state...}, computed_decisions: [{predicate, value, source: "user|default|inferred"}], created_entities: [{type, appId, summary}], skipped: [{type, reason}], next_actions_suggested: [...]}`. Consumers: (a) MCP tools can read the manifest to answer "how was this Collection set up?" without reverse-engineering from the graph; (b) replay automation can re-run the same wizard with the same form state on another instance for templating; (c) provenance-export (RO-Crate / BagIt) carries the manifest as a first-class artifact; (d) AI assistants get a clean view of "the user clicked through this flow" without parsing the activity log. **Pairs with:** task #20 (Create-from-template — entry point already shipped), task #42 (template UX), task #51 (containerless basic mode), Importer's AgentContextIO / ImportManifestIO patterns from v15 (the wizard manifest is the UI-side dual of the importer-side manifest). | M | queued | Design decision needed: does the wizard manifest live as a FileReference on the entity (durable, queryable) or as a separate `:WizardRun` Neo4j node linked to the entity (graph-traversable)? Recommend file-attached: easier to round-trip, cheaper to read. Effort sized for one canonical wizard (Create-from-template) as proof-of-concept; subsequent wizards follow the same shape. |
| SD-WIPE-AND-REGET | **Wipe today's orphan SD containers + re-import SD payloads from source (preferred over redrive).** Operator decision 2026-05-23: rather than re-POST payloads to the existing 4 193 containers (the redrive path), DELETE them and let v15.13 + v15.14 re-create one container per process-step with the source-side SD content. | MFFD-IMPORT-BUG-F | **v15.14 — SD container reuse: one SD container per process-step, not per-Execution.** Surfaced 2026-05-23 by operator clarification + dest-side count probe: MFFD-Dropbox has **4 193** structuredDataContainers created today vs **2 expected** (one for Tapelaying, one for Bridgewelding). Three additions: (a) Pre-flight banner — before iteration, the importer counts every source collection and prints "PRE-FLIGHT TOTALS" with per-step + grand totals. Operators see denominator before any work starts; emitted as `warmup_step:pre_flight_totals` diag event with the full `source_map`. (b) Contained completeness pass — at end of `run_source_mode` the importer aggregates the per-step counters it already maintains (files uploaded/skipped/failed, ts imported/skipped/failed, sd imported/failed, duration_s) into a verdict struct (`_build_completeness_verdict`) and emits a `migration_completeness` diag event plus prints a human-readable banner (`_print_completeness_banner`) showing verdict (PASS / FAIL-PARTIAL / FAIL-EMPTY), per-kind totals, computed rate (DOs/min), and detected flags. Recognised flag shapes include `BUG-E-SHAPE-SD-100PCT-LOSS` (the v15.9-v15.11 signature — file uploads OK but every SD failed), `SD-PARTIAL-LOSS-NEEDS-REDRIVE`, `DO-COUNT-MISMATCH:<step>`, `PARTIAL-KIND-FAILURE:<step>`. (c) Artifact persistence — `mffd-completeness-<session>.json` written to `MFFD_COMPLETENESS_OUT_DIR` (default cwd), and best-effort upload as a `MIGRATION-COMPLETENESS-<SESSION>` DataObject in the destination collection (lineage anchor). No external script needed — completeness lives inside the importer process and uses its own runtime knowledge, no extra source/dest queries. Smoke-tested with synthetic 1400-DO BUG-E shape → correctly classified `FAIL-PARTIAL` + `BUG-E-SHAPE-SD-100PCT-LOSS` flag. **Pairs with:** standalone `mffd-completeness-check.py` (still available for forensic re-verification post-hoc). Triggered by user requests 2026-05-23 *"can you fold total info in importer as well"* + *"also completeness check"* + *"contained process"*. | M | done (v15.13, 2026-05-23) | Compile gate + version canary + verdict-aggregator smoke test ✓. Pure-function aggregator unit-testable. Best-effort upload (does not block on failure). Sibling: post-ingest DB audit MFFD-DB-AUDIT-REAL-DATA. |
| MFFD-DB-AUDIT-REAL-DATA | **Post-ingest DB audit with real MFFD data — antipatterns, bad design, best-practice gaps.** Queued 2026-05-23 by user: *"when we finally ingested data we will run databases audit again with the real data and look for antipatterns, bad design and implement best practices."* Triggered AFTER (a) v15.13 import completes the bridgewelding + tapelaying ingest, (b) MFFD-COMPLETENESS verdict reaches PASS or operator accepts PARTIAL, (c) destination warmed with real-data volumes (thousands of DOs, files in Garage, SDs in Mongo, TS samples in TimescaleDB, semantic annotations in Neo4j). Cross-substrate sweep: Neo4j + PostgreSQL + TimescaleDB + MongoDB + PostGIS + Garage. Builds on prior empty/synthetic-data audit pass (`aidocs/agent-findings/db-schema-research-*.md` + `db-antipatterns-*.md`). Look for: hot-path query patterns that need indexes (Neo4j label-property indexes, Mongo compound indexes, Timescale chunk pruning); Cypher patterns that don't scale (cartesian joins, expanding-bag traversals); SD container collection proliferation in Mongo (one Mongo collection per SD container — at MFFD volume that's potentially 1000+ collections); Garage object naming + bucket layout under real load; PG↔Neo4j duplication seams (where the same fact lives in both); SHACL-shape vs runtime-query mismatch (cf. `feedback_shacl_single_source_of_truth.md`); TS chunk + retention policy fit for MFFD cadence; permission lookup cost at depth. Output: `aidocs/agent-findings/db-audit-post-mffd-real-data.md` + per-substrate sub-findings. Pairs with `feedback_db_review_all_stores.md`. | L | queued | Dependency: v15.13 ingest complete + verdict PASS/PARTIAL accepted. Use the live data — no fixtures, no synthetic seeds. Cross-cutting findings (touch all six substrates) are the highest-value output. |
| MFFD-IMPORT-BUG-E | **v15.12 — fix SD payload BSON-array reject (root cause of 100% StepMetaProcessExecution failure rate).** SHIPPED 2026-05-23 in v15.12. Backend `StructuredDataService.java:53` calls `Document.parse(payload.getPayload())` which MongoDB's BSON model rejects with `readStartDocument...not when CurrentBSONType is ARRAY` when the inner JSON has an array at root. The v15.9-v15.11 importer was hitting this on every `StepMetaProcessExecution` SD upload because that payload IS a list. **Fix:** `upload_structured_payload()` wraps non-dict payloads in `{"items": [...], "_wrapped": "v15.12-bug-e"}` before `_json.dumps()`. Readers consuming MFFD SD payloads must unwrap the single `items` key when `_wrapped` marker present. Diagnosed via destination backend log grep (`f1a0a74d-7436-41a7-8dc6-9d13dc2d883e` reference) → exact exception type → traced to `StructuredDataService.java:53` `Document.parse()` call. **Sibling:** MFFD-IMPORT-COMPLETENESS-CHECK (post-migration verifier so we can confirm the wrap actually landed everything). **Operator action needed:** redrive the SD references already created with empty payloads (ID range 632242..current → all bridgewelding SDs that hit 500 since import started). Either DELETE + recreate or POST again to same /payload (since prior call never landed). Per-DO recovery scriptable from the source 5-tuple (collection + DO + container name → original SD payload). | S | done (v15.12, 2026-05-23) | Wrap fix + version canary + py_compile gate ✓. Cube hot-patch + main commit + manifest publish pending. Backend-side alternative (detect array-root + wrap before Document.parse) tracked as MFFD-SD-BACKEND-WRAP-FALLBACK. |
| MFFD-IMPORT-COMPLETENESS-CHECK | **Post-migration completeness verifier — `mffd-completeness-check.py` v1.0.** SHIPPED 2026-05-23. Standalone Python script (no dependency on the importer module — uses its own thin Client) that compares source vs destination Shepard instances per DataObject and emits a structured completeness report. Per-DO row: existence-in-dest + per-kind ref counts (files / TS / SD / fileBundle / video / image / anomaly / semantic / children) + blocking kinds. Output: machine-readable `mffd-completeness-<session>.json` + human-readable `.md` + uploaded as a first-class `MIGRATION-COMPLETENESS-<session>` DataObject in the destination Collection (lineage anchor for the verification artefact itself). Exit codes 0=PASS / 1=PARTIAL / 2=MISSING-DOS / 3=CONN-FAIL — usable in CI / cron / wrapper-finish hook. Match strategy: `attributes.source_id` → `attributes.source_appId` → `appId` fallback (handles current + future enrichment shapes from MFFD-IMPORT-SOURCE-BY-ATTRS). Failure-class histogram (top 20) + first-50-failing-DOs table in MD output for fast triage. Logs `SUMMARY: {...}` JSON line on stdout for downstream log scraping. | S | done (v1.0, 2026-05-23) | Path: `examples/mffd-showcase/scripts/mffd-completeness-check.py`. | MFFD-IMPORT-DIAG | **v15.11 — structured diagnostic instrumentation for self-diagnosable failures.** SHIPPED 2026-05-23 in v15.11. Adds `DiagSink` class emitting one JSON line per event to stderr (atomic via single `os.write(2, ...)` under module-level lock, ≤4096 bytes = Linux PIPE_BUF), tee'd into the existing log file and mirrored into the existing `Telemetry` channel (best-effort, never breaks emit). New `--diag-mode={quiet,normal,verbose,http-trace}` flag (default `normal`; env `MFFD_DIAG_MODE`). 18 event kinds (startup, warmup_step, source_user_resolved, iter_start/end, do_start/skip/done/error, http_request/response, worker_pool, jwt_status, manifest_poll, state_save, telemetry_flush, summary, shutdown). Auto-classified diagnostic hints from a pure-function `classify_error(status, body)` → 9 hint codes (jwt-expired-or-rotated, permission-denied, not-found, conflict, rate-limited, bean-validation, client-error, server-side, timeout-or-network) with human-readable actions. Per-DO correlation id (`<step>:<src_do_id>`) ties every related event together. Non-2xx http responses ALWAYS emit regardless of mode — failure signal must not be filterable. Credential masking (`mask_credential` → `sha256:<first-12-hex>`) with explicit plaintext-leak guard test. Shutdown event carries the final 60s rolling-window summary. 36 new pytest cases in `tests/test_diag.py` (wire shape, 8-thread atomic-write concurrency, mode gating, all 9 error classes, JWT decode well-formed + malformed, credential mask + leak guard, summary aggregation, payload truncation, PIPE_BUF overflow marker, telemetry-mirror best-effort, version constant). Pattern card: `aidocs/integrations/95 §Pattern 19`. Closes the "2 AM debugging requires code spelunking" failure mode by making logs alone sufficient to diagnose any of: wire-shape errors, 401/403/404/409/429, rate limits, worker deadlock, JWT expiry, lock contention, state-file inconsistency, source-side missing content, Quarkus bean-validation violations. | M | done (v15.11, 2026-05-23) | DiagSink ✓ + 18 event kinds ✓ + classifier ✓ + masking ✓ + atomic-write concurrency test ✓. Sibling row: LOG-AS-PROV-ARTEFACT (dest-side consumption of diagnostic events into PROV-O `:Activity`). |

| UX-REVERT-MUTATIONS | **First-class "undo" for data mutations — user-facing revert of changes / mutation passes.** Companion to the Goldilocks-shaping principle (`project_mffd_dest_backfill_pass.md`, `project_dataset_forging.md`): if mutations are iterative ("juuuuuuuust right"), then UNDO must be first-class. Every mutation that lands via the v2 API is recorded as a typed `:Activity` (PROV-O) with input/output state references; the UI exposes a "history" panel per DataObject / Collection / Container showing N most recent mutations with one-click "revert this change" (returns to the pre-mutation state) and bulk "revert N passes" (back to S(N-k)). Plays nice with the snapshot chain S0→S1→...→Sn that the back-fill pattern produces. Pairs with PV1a payload version history (already shipped — extends from "file payload versions" to "attribute + reference + structure mutations"). Probably needs a v2 endpoint `POST /v2/{resource}/{appId}/revert?to=activityAppId` + `GET /v2/{resource}/{appId}/mutations` (list). | L | queued | Source: 2026-05-23 user flag ("for backlog, easy way to revert changes / mutations for users"). Companion to MFFD-IMPORTER-DATASET-CAPTURE + the dest backfill pattern. Critical for trusting AI-driven mutation passes — user can experiment + back out safely. EN 9100 audit angle: the revert trail IS the audit trail. |

| NETCDF1 | **Plugin: shepard-plugin-netcdf — NetCDF / CF-conventions payload kind.** Self-describing multidimensional arrays with embedded metadata; dominant in atmospheric science, oceanography, climate, AFP thermal-trace exports, CFD post-processing. Build as `shepard-plugin-netcdf` (plugin-first per CLAUDE.md §2 PayloadKind heuristic). Library: UCAR netCDF-Java (BSD-3-Clause) for read, h5netcdf or netCDF4-python for sidecar tooling. Browse: dimensions + variables + attributes per file via REST. Stream: HDF5-S3 access pattern (netCDF-4 is HDF5-based — same chunked-streaming substrate as A5). CF-compliance check on upload (warn don't reject). Companion to HDF5 plugin (A5 shipped) — NetCDF is "HDF5 with conventions"; in many cases the same file unpacks via either lens. **🛈 Clarification 2026-05-23 (user flag "none are for direct reuse - informational only"):** The UNAS code-drop projects are **informational only** — patterns + design references + field-confirmation that ZLP needs the integration shape. Do NOT propose direct code-reuse / dependency adoption from these zips. They inform the *shape* of what to build, not the *substrate* to build on. Treat the listed projects as "see how others solved this" rather than "import this library." Reuse-before-reimplement still applies — but the reuse decision goes through fresh upstream OSS evaluation, not the UNAS snapshot.

| PERM-SYSTEM-REVIEW | **Permission system review — consistency, inheritance, ACL vs RBAC vs alternatives.** Today's Shepard permissions are a per-entity ACL bolted on: each entity (Collection, FileContainer, DataObject, ...) carries `{owner, permissionType: Private\|Public, reader[], writer[], readerGroupIds[], writerGroupIds[], manager[]}`. **Live failure modes observed 2026-05-23** (RoboDK dropbox setup): (a) FileContainer created via REST defaults to `Private` despite being inside a `Public` Collection — no inheritance; (b) DataObject has no per-entity permissions endpoint (`GET /collections/{id}/dataObjects/{did}/permissions` 404) so write authorization is unclear / inconsistent with FileContainer pattern; (c) `createFileReference` fails opaquely when either DO or FC denies write — error toast literally reads "Error while createFileReference:" with empty message after colon (the UX-FRIENDLY-ERRORS symptom); (d) ~~per task #148, DataObject creation doesn't seed a Permissions record at all, causing 403 cascades~~ **CORRECTED 2026-05-24** (see `aidocs/agent-findings/bug-148-do-perms-seeded-2026-05-24.md`): DataObjects are **designed** to not seed own Permissions; access inherits from parent Collection via `PermissionsService.isAccessAllowedForDataObjectAppId` (lines 291-329 of `PermissionsService.java`). Live verified all 17,149 DOs lack `:Permissions` and all writes succeed via the parent-Collection walk (HTTP 200/201, zero 403s). The RoboDK 403 cascades trace to sub-bullet (a) — FileContainer not inheriting parent Collection's `Public` setting — not anything DO-related. **BUG-148 / task #148 → close as works-as-designed.** **Design question to resolve**: (1) **Pure ACL** (current shape, fix inheritance + add DO endpoint) — minimal change, retains owner-centric model, but every entity carries its own list; doesn't scale to project-level orgs. (2) **RBAC** (roles: viewer, contributor, curator, admin; scoped to Collection) — projects assign roles, members inherit. Clean for institutional use; loses fine-grained per-DO override. (3) **RBAC + ABAC overrides (PBAC, policy-based)** — RBAC as default, per-entity policy lets `embargo_until: 2027-01-01` or `accessRights: restricted access` short-circuit role grants. Best fit for FAIR + EN 9100 needs (embargo, license-gated access, NCR-confidentiality), but complex. (4) **Capability-based / Macaroons** — bearer tokens carry scoped capabilities (read coll-X-until-2027 + write fc-626776). Composable, delegatable, but breaks the "user-in-list" UI assumption. **Recommendation to investigate** (audit before implementation): RBAC core + ABAC overlay (option 3). Default role grants from Collection; per-entity policies layer on license / embargo / access-rights from LIC1. Pairs with TPL10 DQR (DataQualityRequirement) which can carry policy. The 5 acceptance lenses: (A) auditor-ready audit trail per access decision (PROV1a captures the decision; the role + policy at decision time); (B) onboarding a new contributor takes ≤ 2 clicks (assign role, done); (C) embargo enforcement is a property not a one-off ACL entry; (D) inheritance: child inherits parent unless explicitly overridden; (E) all four UI badges (🌐 Public / 👁 Restricted / 🔒 Closed / ⏱ Embargoed) compute deterministically from role+policy without per-entity ACL lookup. Audit deliverable: `aidocs/platform/<n>-permission-system-review.md` with reuse survey (existing FAIR-aware ACL libraries: Keycloak Authorization, OPA, Cedar (AWS, Apache-2.0) — Cedar particularly notable as it's purpose-built for ABAC-on-RBAC), prior art (CKAN dataset access, Coscine + RWTH; Dataverse role assignments; openBIS spaces+projects), and decision matrix. | L | queued | Source: 2026-05-23 user flag with screenshot evidence ("permission system review for more consistency - inheritance, discuss ACL or RBAC or alternatives") + live failure on RoboDK FC. Pairs with #148 (Permissions bug) + UX-FRIENDLY-ERRORS (the opaque error) + LIC1 (license field needs policy enforcement) + TPL10 (DQR). |

| BUG-UI-FILEREF-EMPTY-OIDS | **UI bug: createFileReference POSTs with empty `fileOids` array.** Live repro 2026-05-23: user opens DataObject → "Add data reference" → picks a 12.1 MB .rdk file → picks existing FileContainer → clicks Upload → 400 `fileOids must not be empty`. The 2-step backend flow is: (a) POST file content to `/shepard/api/fileContainers/{cid}/payload` returning fileOid, (b) POST `{name, fileContainerId, fileOids: [oid]}` to `/collections/{cid}/dataObjects/{did}/fileReferences`. Either step (a) is failing silently and step (b) fires anyway, OR step (b) doesn't await the step (a) Promise. Frontend file: search `frontend/components/dialog/AddDataReferenceDialog.vue` or similar; also `frontend/composables/api/useFileReferences.ts`. Likely fix: chain `await uploadToContainer(file) → const oid = response.oid → createFileReference({fileOids: [oid]})`. UX-FRIENDLY-ERRORS would surface this honestly (the error toast literally truncates to "Error while createFileReference:"). | M | queued | Source: 2026-05-23 screenshot evidence + curl-traced 400 reproduction. Workaround: 2-step curl-upload (literal command in commit body). Pairs with UX-FRIENDLY-ERRORS + #135 file upload progress + PERM-SYSTEM-REVIEW (this is the kind of failure mode the permission audit must include). |

| LOG-ENHANCEMENT | **Enhance logging on Shepard for debuggability.** Today most v2 endpoints log at minimal verbosity; constraint-violation rejections + 4xx responses don't include actionable context (which user, which collection, which payload shape). Audit shape: (a) structured-log every request boundary (method, path, user appId, http status, latency, body-shape-hash) at INFO; (b) every Activity-mutating call gets DEBUG-level pre/post-state diffs (the data needed for the prov-artefact angle below); (c) admin-facing log viewer under `/v2/admin/logs?since=...&level=...` (per UX-aided diagnose-by-self) — gates behind instance-admin role; (d) wire to VictoriaLogs sidecar (LOGSTORE design `aidocs/integrations/94`); (e) sensible defaults: INFO in prod, DEBUG togglable per-request via `X-Debug-Token` header for support sessions. Pairs with #115 (comprehensive logging pass for createGitReference). | M | queued | Source: 2026-05-23 user flag ("backlog item to enhance logging on shepard so debugging becomes easier"). Pairs with UX-FRIENDLY-ERRORS + LOGSTORE design. |
| BUG-148-DESIGN-ASSERT-TEST | **Lock the DataObject-permissions inheritance contract into a regression-anti-test.** BUG-148 (2026-05-24) was a misdiagnosis ("DO creation should seed a Permissions record"); the real design is that DOs inherit from parent Collection via `PermissionsService.isAccessAllowedForDataObjectAppId` (lines 291-329) and the 3-arg fallback overload (lines 276-289). Add a JUnit on `DataObjectServiceTest` asserting (a) a freshly-created DO has NO direct `:Permissions` node (`permissionsDAO.findByEntityNeo4jId(doId) == null`), AND (b) `permissionsService.isAccessTypeAllowedForUser(doId, AccessType.Write, currentUser)` returns true via the walk. The test is the anti-regression — it fails if a future agent tries to "fix" BUG-148 by adding a per-DO Permissions seed. Pairs with PERM-SYSTEM-REVIEW (the test asserts the *current* contract; PERM-SYSTEM-REVIEW is free to change it). | XS | queued | Source: `aidocs/agent-findings/bug-148-do-perms-seeded-2026-05-24.md` §Test results. |
| V14-WHERE-CLAUSE-TIGHTEN | **V14 orphan-permissions backfill WHERE clause is too broad.** `V14__Backfill_orphan_permissions.cypher` line 44-45 matches `(e:BasicEntity) WHERE NOT (e)-[:has_permissions]->(:Permissions)` — but DataObject + BasicReference ARE BasicEntity nodes and are **designed** to not have direct Permissions (inheritance from parent Collection per `PermissionsService.isAccessAllowedForDataObjectAppId`). If an operator ever sets `shepard.permissions.default-owner` on a graph with existing DataObjects or BasicReferences, V14 will attach Permissions to all of them, silently breaking the inheritance walk (since the walk's null-check at PermissionsService:278 short-circuits the moment a direct Permissions node exists). Tighten the WHERE clause to whitelist the entity types that ARE supposed to have direct Permissions: `WHERE (e:Collection OR e:StructuredDataContainer OR e:FileContainer OR e:TimeseriesContainer) AND NOT (e)-[:has_permissions]->(:Permissions)`. Ship as V15 migration (V14 is already applied on prod) + add a `:_ShepardMigrationContext.label-allowlist` admin override for plugins to extend. | S | queued | Source: `aidocs/agent-findings/bug-148-do-perms-seeded-2026-05-24.md` §What surprised me. Pairs with PERM-SYSTEM-REVIEW + BUG-148-DESIGN-ASSERT-TEST. |
| LOG-AS-PROV-ARTEFACT | **Shepard logs (processed) as PROV-O artefact describing mutations.** Distinct from LOG-ENHANCEMENT but compose-able with it: every Shepard log record that describes a mutation (POST/PUT/PATCH/DELETE) becomes a typed `:Activity` in the prov substrate — `prov:wasAttributedTo` (user), `prov:used` (input refs), `prov:generated` (output refs), `prov:atTime` (timestamp), `shepard:operation` (verb+path), `shepard:resultStatus` (http). Processing pipeline: VictoriaLogs sidecar ingests raw logs → a normaliser (plugin? sidecar? in-tree filter?) extracts mutation events → writes :Activity nodes to Neo4j. **Recursion**: every Shepard mutation thus gets two trails — the raw log (operational) and the typed prov node (semantic). Activity diff = log diff projected through PROV-O. The case-study value: a queryable "what actually changed and why" surface that survives long after the log retention window. Pairs with PROV1a (ProvenanceCaptureFilter — already captures mutations, but as filter-time records, not log-processed) — open question: dual-write vs. consolidate to one path. | L | queued | Source: 2026-05-23 user flag ("shepard logs (maybe processed) as prov artefact describing mutations"). Pairs with LOG-ENHANCEMENT + LOGSTORE design + PROV1a + the f(ai)²R recursion principle. |

| MOBILE-PWA | **Shepard frontend as a Progressive Web App (PWA) for mobile.** Researchers + auditors increasingly check Shepard from phones / tablets — esp. on the shop floor (per the manufacturing-quality persona's ruggedized terminal requirement). | VIEW-RECOMMENDER | **AI-assisted view recommender: "what should I look at next?" by context + user needs.** A Collection page surfaces dozens of DataObjects + payload kinds; a researcher arriving cold doesn't know where to start. | SUST-AI-LOG | **Log AI-inference energy + CO₂ alongside Shepard's own compute footprint.** SUST1 (`aidocs/sustainability/01-methodology.md`) logs container compute; the AI co-pilot's inference cost is currently invisible. Pairs with SUST1 + project_ai_plugin_config + the f(ai)²r recursion principle. |

| HTML-TO-MD-MIGRATION | **Migrate all rendered fields from HTML to Markdown — combined with block-editor (editor.js / BlockNote) research.** User flags 2026-05-23: ("move from html rendering to markdown in all fields /migrate") + ("combine with editor js research"). The migration target is not "markdown text in a textarea" but a **shape-driven block editor** where each block is a typed Shepard individual, serialised to markdown for storage. **Phase A — data migration**: (a) inventory HTML-bearing fields backend (`description`, `notes`, attributes, lab-journal entries, ref comments) + frontend (`v-html`, contenteditable, rich-text); (b) HTML → markdown via `turndown` on read OR one-shot Cypher/SQL; (c) markdown sanitiser tests (XSS, scripts, styles, malicious links); (d) export round-trip test. **Phase B — block editor**: (e) pick base — **editor.js** (MIT, flexible blocks) vs **BlockNote** (MIT, Notion-flavour UX) — full reuse-survey per `feedback_reuse_before_reimplement.md`; (f) each block type maps to a typed Shepard individual (heading / paragraph / table → existing TableContainer / code / image → file-reference / ts-chart → embedded TS view / shepard-ref → any artefact); (g) mode A form-shapes from SHACL templates + mode B free-text; (h) per-block `fair2r:modeOfProduction` + author + timestamp attribution; (i) lossless markdown round-trip; (j) admin-configurable block-type registry. Subsumes `project_block_editor.md`. Migration mode: backward-read → forward-write → drop HTML. | L | queued | Source: 2026-05-23 user flags. Pairs with PV1a (markdown diffs cleanly), UX-FRIENDLY-ERRORS, LABJOURNAL-SCIENTIFIC-TWITTER (the labjournal IS the canonical consumer of the new block editor). |

| LABJOURNAL-SCIENTIFIC-TWITTER | **Lab journal as scientific twitter — direct references to Shepard artefacts of all types; render specifics supplied by plugins; AI agents can join the convo.** User flags 2026-05-23: ("labjournal should be a scientific twitter with direct references to shepard artifacts (of all types - specifics should be supplied by plugins responsible)") + ("maybe even agents ca join the convo"). The shape: every lab-journal entry is a short post (twitter-style, but no length limit) authored by either a human OR an AI agent (both with f(ai)²r attribution). Entries can **directly reference** any Shepard artefact — DataObject, Collection, FileReference, TimeseriesReference, StructuredDataReference, GitReference, AAS submodel, ImageBundle frame, anything a plugin contributes as a `PayloadKind`. The **render specifics for each reference type come from the plugin responsible** for that PayloadKind (per the PayloadKind SPI — image plugin renders thumbnail-with-link, TS plugin renders live-sparkline-snippet, GitReference renders commit-shape, etc.) — labjournal core knows nothing about how to render a TS chart; it asks the TS plugin. **Threading**: entries can reply to other entries (twitter-style); branch into discussion sub-threads; pin pinnable posts; mention users (`@kreb_fl`) + agents (`@claude-opus-4-7`). **Agent participation**: AI agents post into the labjournal under their model identity with mandatory `🤖 Posted by` transparency line (per `feedback_role_agents_file_issues.md` extended pattern); the agent's reasoning per post is captured + cite-able. **Agent capabilities in-thread** (per user flag 2026-05-23 "assisting in research questions - ordering thoughts - reformatting extracting semantic anchors"): (1) **research-question assistance** — agent surfaces related artefacts, related literature (via paper-search MCP), open-question gaps; (2) **thought-ordering** — agent suggests reorderings of a chain of posts, identifies missing transitions, surfaces implicit assumptions; (3) **reformatting** — agent polishes markdown formatting, suggests block-type replacements (e.g. "this list reads better as a table"), maintains house-style; (4) **semantic-anchor extraction** — agent reads free-text posts and proposes typed annotations from the active ontology (CHAMEO / Material OWL / m4i / domain-vocabulary), surfacing them as user-acceptable suggestions per the f(ai)²r five-rung acceptance ladder. Each agent suggestion lands as a NEW post in the thread (not an inline edit) — preserving the conversational shape + the human's final-decision authority. **Composition**: built on top of HTML-TO-MD-MIGRATION's block editor — each post IS a block-editor document with first-class artefact-reference blocks. Replaces the existing lab-journal entry shape (which is plain markdown today per J1 chain). | XL | queued | Source: 2026-05-23 user flags. Pairs with HTML-TO-MD-MIGRATION (block editor substrate), TPL9 (f(ai)²r AI provenance), PERSONA-ISSUES-FROM-AUDIT (the AI-can-post-with-transparency pattern), J1d (lab-journal entry history panel + diff viewer — the new shape needs new viewers), NTF1 (notifications: who got mentioned). Cross-references `project_block_editor.md` (Twitter-hybrid attribution per block — already in memory; this row makes it concrete for labjournal). |

## FAIR4-* — FAIR4ML × FAIR-for-AI × f(ai)²r alignment

Rows opened by the 2026-05-23 comparative survey
`aidocs/semantics/fair4ml-fair4ai-fai2r-2026-05-23.md`. Each one closes
a specific predicate-level integration gap between f(ai)²r (this fork's
PROV-O extension; `noheton/f-ai-r`) and the RDA FAIR4ML schema.org
extension (`w3id.org/fair4ml`). Sequence them after PROMPT1 (the
PromptLog substrate is the canonical f(ai)²r consumer in the fork).

| ID | Description | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| FAIR4-SURVEY | **Comparative survey done — `aidocs/semantics/fair4ml-fair4ai-fai2r-2026-05-23.md`.** Nine-dimension comparison (authority / scope / maturity / lead institutions / predicate count / RDF / SHACL / EU policy / lifecycle stage). Conclusion: f(ai)²r and FAIR4ML are complementary along orthogonal axes (authoring vs distribution); the thesis posture is A+B (gap-filling + lifecycle-stage complementarity), not C (competition). | S | **feature-defined 2026-05-23** | Source doc landed. Ten follow-on rows below close the predicate-level alignment work. |
| FAIR4-NS-FREEZE | **Freeze the canonical f(ai)²r namespace to `https://noheton.org/f-ai-r/ns#`.** The fork uses `https://noheton.github.io/f-ai-r/ns#` in `aidocs/semantics/99-promptlog-design.md` line 579 (and downstream SHACL shapes); the canonical repo uses `https://noheton.org/f-ai-r/ns#` in `doc/provenance.ttl`. Diverged namespace = future merge cost. Coordinate with VIEWS-AS-SHAPES-CANONICAL-IRIS (#1137) — same shape of fix, different vocab. | S | queued | Bridges with: VIEWS-AS-SHAPES-CANONICAL-IRIS (#1137), FAIR4-SHACL-COMPLIANCE. |
| FAIR4-BRIDGE-ONTOLOGY | **Ship a small bridge ontology at `aidocs/semantics/fair4ml-bridge.ttl`** that imports `fair4ml:`, `fair2r:`, `m4i:`, `prov:`, `schema:` and declares the composition rules: `fair4ml:MLModel rdfs:subClassOf prov:Entity`; an MLModel can be the `prov:generated` of an `m4i:ProcessingStep` (training run) which `prov:wasInformedBy` a `fair2r:AuthoringPass` (LLM hyperparameter conversation); `shp:MLModelCollection rdfs:subClassOf fair2r:Manuscript, schema:CreativeWork`. This is the alignment artefact a peer reviewer reads. | M | queued | Pairs with M4I-d (m4i × f(ai)²r bridge), `aidocs/semantics/94 §M4I-d`. |
| FAIR4-SHACL-COMPLIANCE | **SHACL shape `shp:Fair4mlMLModelShape`** validating a Shepard Collection-tagged-as-MLModel against FAIR4ML v0.1.0 minimum-metadata expectations (`fair4ml:mlTask`, `fair4ml:trainedOn`, `fair4ml:intendedUse`, `fair4ml:modelRisksBiasLimitations`, `schema:author`, `schema:license`). FAIR4ML v0.1.0 ships predicate types but no shapes; this is a contribution back to the RDA FAIR4ML IG. Affects every Collection landing for every user. | S | ✅ **shipped** 2026-05-24 | Frontend-only — endpoint exists and 404 was intentional API design ("not watching"). `useCollectionWatch.refresh()` now uses `listWatchers` + `MeApi.getMe()` (both always-200). `/me` backend endpoint untouched (separate legitimate use). | UI-011e | **`# DOs` column shows 0 everywhere on `/collections` list.** Surfaced by UX Scrutinizer 2026-05-24. **Root cause turned out to be different from the task hypothesis:** `GET /v2/collections` (CollectionV2Rest → CollectionDAO) already returns correct counts on live (LUMEN=17, MFFD-Dropbox=8514, Home=3). The frontend `/collections` page does NOT call that endpoint — it calls `SearchApi.searchCollections` → `POST /shepard/api/search/collections` → `SearchDAO.findCollections`, whose `emitCollectionReturnPart` used `Neighborhood.ESSENTIAL` (= `path=(c)-[*0..1]->(n) WHERE n:Permission OR n:User`). ESSENTIAL never walks DataObjects, so `CollectionIO.dataObjectIds[]` came back empty on every search result. Fix: flip the collection projection to `Neighborhood.EVERYTHING` (depth 1) — the same neighborhood `CollectionDAO.findAllCollectionsByShepardId` already uses successfully in production. Container / User / UserGroup `emit*ReturnPart` helpers stay on ESSENTIAL (their cells don't expose nested-entity counts). | S | ✅ **shipped** (worktree UI-011e) | UI-011 follow-up; ships before UI-011a..d because it's broken not deferred. JUnit: extended `SearchDAOTest.findCollectionsTest` to assert the new Cypher + added `findCollectionsHydratesDataObjects_UI011e` as regression guard. Vitest unnecessary — no frontend change (field name `dataObjectIds` already matched). Playwright e2e: `e2e/tests/ui-011e-do-count-shows.spec.ts` asserts LUMEN + MFFD-Dropbox rows show non-zero `# DOs`. Finding doc: `aidocs/agent-findings/ui-011e-do-count-fix-2026-05-24.md`. |
| UX-PATTERN-A | **Loading-state leaks as error (red toast on cold load).** Surfaced by UX Scrutinizer 2026-05-24 (`aidocs/agent-findings/ux-scrutinizer-workflows-2026-05-24.md` §"Pattern A"). On every Phase-2/3/5 workflow during cold load the UI flashed a red error toast claiming data was unavailable — actually `handleError()` was emitting on `AbortError` (route changed mid-flight) and on `401 Unauthorized` (which the auth-refresh middleware silently handles). Fix: two early-returns at the top of `frontend/utils/errorBus.ts::handleError` filter both classes; both still log to console at WARN so real bugs remain debuggable. 7-test Vitest regression guard added (`tests/unit/errorBus.test.ts`). | XS | ✅ **shipped** (worktree UX-POLISH-2026-05-24) | Finding doc: `aidocs/agent-findings/ux-polish-bundle-2026-05-24.md`. Live verified via `e2e/tests/ux-polish-2026-05-24.spec.ts` (Pattern A test polls toast every 100 ms for 2 s, asserts never appears). |
| UX-PATTERN-E | **Sidebar sibling-nav under-promoted.** Surfaced by UX Scrutinizer 2026-05-24 (`aidocs/agent-findings/ux-scrutinizer-workflows-2026-05-24.md` §"Pattern E"). The Contents tree IS the sibling navigator (and supports chevron-expand into investigation sub-trees) but first-time users don't realise it. Fix: info icon + tooltip next to the Contents header in `CollectionSidebar.vue` reading "Click any DataObject to jump between siblings. Use the chevron to expand sub-trees" + a sentence in `docs/help/collection-lineage.md` mirroring it. | XS | ✅ **shipped** (worktree UX-POLISH-2026-05-24) | Finding doc: `aidocs/agent-findings/ux-polish-bundle-2026-05-24.md`. |
| UX-PATTERN-F | **Page titles don't include the entity name.** Surfaced by UX Scrutinizer 2026-05-24 (`aidocs/agent-findings/ux-scrutinizer-workflows-2026-05-24.md` §"Pattern F"). Every Collection / DO / Container page had `useHead({ title })` called **inside a watcher** with string-concat + nullish coercion → tab title rendered as `undefined \| shepard` on cold load and leaked a new head entry on every fetch. Patterns: `<Collection.name> — shepard` / `<DO.name> · <Collection.name> — shepard` / `<Container.name> (Files\|Timeseries\|Structured Data\|Spatial Data) — shepard` + sensible fallbacks for the pre-load tick. | XS | ✅ **shipped** (worktree UX-POLISH-2026-05-24) | Finding doc: `aidocs/agent-findings/ux-polish-bundle-2026-05-24.md`. | UX-Q-PARAM | **`/search?q=X` URL param was ignored + header-search "See all results" dropped the query.** Pasting a link with `?q=foo` landed on search but the field stayed empty; the header search dropdown's footer link navigated to bare `/search`, discarding the user's typed query. Fix (two parts): (1) `pages/search/index.vue` reads `?q=` and translates it to a `name contains <value>` JSON query, then runs the search — `?searchQuery=` wins over `?q=` when both present. Logic extracted to `utils/searchQueryFromParams.ts` for unit-testability (8-test Vitest). (2) `components/layout/HeaderBar.vue` — the dropdown's "See all results" `:to` binding + the Enter handler in `onEnterPressed()` now pass `query: { q }` so the round-trip works. | XS | ✅ **shipped** (worktree UX-POLISH-2026-05-24) | Bundled with UX-PATTERN-A/E/F because all four are short and don't conflict. ## CRIT-2026-05-24-* — Critical operational risks

| ID | description | effort | status | notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| ~~CRIT-LOMBOK-APT~~ | **RETRACTED 2026-05-24** — false alarm caused by local working-directory pollution. Three pre-existing dirty mods to `Collection.java` / `DataObjectIO.java` / `SparqlQueryValidator.java` were carried in canonical `/opt/shepard` since session start; the dirty WD made Lombok APT fail. Agent worktrees (`git worktree add` → clean HEAD checkout) build fine — verified by reproducing `mvn clean compile -DskipTests` in `/opt/shepard/.claude/worktrees/agent-*/backend` → green. Three subsequent worktree-isolated agents (UI-011e, OPS-MIGRATION-HEALTHCHECK, RDM-001) all built + deployed + smoked 25/25 from canonical-main-equivalent state. The PROV-resolver agent's report was accurate-for-their-moment but conflated transient cherry-pick state with a main-branch bug. | XS | ✅ **resolved (false alarm)** | Lesson kept as CRIT-SMOKE-NOT-CATCHING-BUILD-BREAK below. Operator note: the three dirty session-original files are still in `/opt/shepard` WD; `git stash` or `git checkout HEAD -- <files>` to restore main if not actively worked on. |
| CRIT-SMOKE-NOT-CATCHING-BUILD-BREAK | **Smoke endpoint passes against a stale running image even when a fresh `mvn clean compile` is broken.** This is how CRIT-LOMBOK-APT hid for a full session. Fix: chain `make build-backend` as a hard prerequisite of `make smoke` (or add a `make smoke-with-build` target that's the default), so a broken main can't deploy "successfully". | S | ✅ **shipped** 2026-05-24 | OPS hygiene bundle. `smoke: build-backend` now in `Makefile`. Self-test caught a probe-injected error AND surfaced a real `TargetEntityResolver.resolve(String)` duplicate-method break sitting on main — filed as `CRIT-MAIN-BROKEN-TARGETENTITYRESOLVER-DUPLICATE` below. See `aidocs/agent-findings/ops-hygiene-bundle-2026-05-24.md`. |
| CRIT-WORKTREE-DOCKER-CACHE | **`make redeploy-frontend` reports success but ships a STALE image from agent worktrees.** Surfaced by UX-Pattern-D agent 2026-05-24: their first `make redeploy-frontend` returned green smoke 25/25 but the live frontend still served the old code. Recovery required `rm -rf .output .nuxt && npm run build && docker build && docker compose up -d --force-recreate frontend`. Suspected: docker layer cache + Nuxt `.output` cache + dev-mode hot-swap container retention combine to mask the staleness. The authoritative live-deploy verify command is `docker exec infrastructure-frontend-1 grep -l <new-testid> /app/server/chunks/build/*.mjs` — chain into `make smoke` or a new `make verify-frontend-deploy` target so it can't repeat. Same family as CRIT-SMOKE-NOT-CATCHING-BUILD-BREAK above (smoke probes running image not fresh code). | M | ✅ **shipped** 2026-05-24 | OPS hygiene bundle. Resolved as a sibling of MK-REDEPLOY-FORCE-RECREATE — `--force-recreate <service>` now folded into every `redeploy*` Makefile target, which closes the docker-cache trap. `verify-frontend-deploy` sentinel-check target deliberately deferred per the OPS-bundle task brief ("--force-recreate alone closes 80%"). |

## SM1a — User-configurable orphan-data retention per container (DEFAULT 1 YEAR)

| ID | description | effort | status | notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| SM1a | **Per-container user-configurable retention for non-referenced data, default 1 year, with notification warnings.** Researcher decides on a per-container basis (or accepts the instance-admin default) how long non-referenced data lives before deletion. The `INTEGRITY RULE` from `feedback_referenced_data_infinite_retention.md` still holds — referenced data is never deleted. Only data with `refs=0 AND payload>0 AND not in active job state` is subject to the retention clock. **Default 1 year** (revises the prior SM1 design memory which had `infinite grace`; rationale: most operators don't actually want indefinite orphan accumulation; explicit-opt-in for "infinite" is the safer default-OFF posture). **Per-container fields** on TS / File / SD containers: `orphan_retention_days: int` (NULL = use instance default, 0 = delete-on-next-sweep, -1 = infinite), `orphan_retention_owner_notified_at: timestamp?`. **Notification cadence**: nag at 30d / 7d / 1d before deletion (NTF1 dep), one final "deleted N items" on actual deletion. **UI**: a Retention card on each container detail page with the current setting + a select with explicit options (Infinite / 1 year / 90 days / 30 days / Delete-on-orphan); plus an instance-admin landing tile to set the instance default. **Audit**: every retention-driven deletion lands in `:Activity` with `:RetentionSweep` source kind. **Acceptance**: a researcher can opt into infinite, accept the 1-year default, or tighten to 30d; gets the nag notifications; sees deletions in the activity trail. | L | queued | Revises `project_storage_management.md` default (infinite → 1 year). Depends on: NTF1 (notifications, in design), `:Activity` source-kind extension. Frontend + backend + Cypher migration (per-container retention fields) + scheduled-job (sweep). Update aidocs/34 + 44 + model-inventory. **Operator-facing default change — document loudly in v6.x release notes.** |
| SM1a-RUNBOOK | **Operator runbook for retention policy** — `docs/admin/runbooks/orphan-retention-policy.md`. Covers: where to set the instance default, what the per-container override does, how the nag cadence fires, how to recover a container from delete-on-next-sweep state in the brief window before it fires, audit-trail query (`MATCH (a:Activity {sourceKind: 'RetentionSweep'})`), and how to opt out entirely (set instance default to infinite). Sibling to `docs/admin/runbooks/restore-tsdb-container-neo4j-shadow.md`. | S | queued | Same-PR as SM1a per `feedback_admin_runbooks_pattern.md`. |

## PROV-2026-05-24-* — Provenance trail completeness gaps

Source: `aidocs/agent-findings/rdm-004-provenance-empty-fix-2026-05-24.md` (closes RDM-2026-05-24-004). Root-cause analysis showed the LUMEN DO Provenance panel renders an empty list because 99.93 % of recorded Activities have `targetKind=NULL`/`targetAppId=NULL` — the capture filter's path resolver fails on subresource paths and on v1 numeric-id paths. The empty-state copy fix (Bucket D) shipped in the same PR; the structural pieces are tracked below.

| ID | Item | effort | status | notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| PROV-EMPTY-STATE-COPY | **`DataObjectProvLog.vue` empty state now distinguishes "no events recorded" from "filter hid everything".** Adds an optional `hint` prop on `EmptyListIcon` and two computed branches (extracted to `frontend/utils/provenanceEmptyState.ts` for testability). Closes the trust-killer signal: a researcher landing on a DO with zero activities now reads a precise explanation of capture scope instead of a suspect empty panel. | XS | ✅ **shipped** 2026-05-24 | Frontend-only, <50 LOC. Vitest passes. See findings doc above. |
| PROV-RESOLVER-PATHWALK | **`TargetEntityResolver` walks the path right-to-left for the deepest `(kind, id)` pair instead of insisting on the tail.** Subresource creates now attach to the newly-minted entity, not its parent. Pre-fix: `POST /v2/collections/<COLL-uuid>/dataobjects` recorded the Collection UUID with kind `DataObject` (wrong target). Post-fix: walks right-to-left for `(knownPlural, idLike)` pairs; unknown plurals no longer fall back to title-casing — verb-shaped segments like `payload`/`diff`/`detect-anomalies` can't pollute `targetKind` any more. Pure refactor split: `PathTargetParser` (static parser) + `TargetEntityResolver` (CDI bean wiring the parser to numeric lookup). | M | ✅ **shipped** 2026-05-24 | Closes RDM-2026-05-24-004 bucket B. Same PR as PROV-V1-NUMERIC-LOOKUP. See `aidocs/agent-findings/prov-resolver-fix-2026-05-24.md`. |
| PROV-V1-NUMERIC-LOOKUP | **Capture-time resolution of `/shepard/api/...` numeric IDs → appIds via a generic `EntityAppIdLookup` helper.** Single parameterised Cypher (`MATCH (n:<Label>) WHERE n.shepardId=$id ...`) over the static label allow-list; deviates from the brief's per-DAO method shape because all targets share `AbstractEntity` (carries `appId`) + `VersionableEntity` (carries `shepardId`), so one helper covers every kind with zero entity-file edits. On miss the Activity lands with `targetKind` set + `targetAppId=null` — capture is never blocked. The optional backfill is split off as `PROV-BACKFILL-MIGRATION`. | L | ✅ **shipped** 2026-05-24 | Closes RDM-2026-05-24-004 bucket C. Same PR as PROV-RESOLVER-PATHWALK. See findings doc. |
| PROV-BACKFILL-MIGRATION | **One-off backfill of the ~280 K orphaned `:Activity` rows whose `targetKind=NULL`.** Implementation should re-use the production `PathTargetParser` from Java (not re-implement string parsing in Cypher), call `EntityAppIdLookup` for each parsed `(kind, numericId)` pair, and write the result back via `apoc.periodic.iterate` (batched, idempotent). Acceptance: post-migration `MATCH (a:Activity) WHERE a.targetKind IS NULL RETURN count(a)` drops by ≥ 250 K. Optional rollback `V**_R__backfill_activity_targets.cypher` clears the back-filled fields. Split from PROV-V1-NUMERIC-LOOKUP to keep this PR shippable; only recovers historic seed traffic. | M | queued | Not blocking; the resolver fix already prevents the bug recurring for new writes. |
| PROV-CAPTURE-READS-DECISION | **Decide whether `shepard.provenance.capture-reads` flips from `false` to `true` for `/v2/...` paths.** Current default is off per `aidocs/55 §4` (read-volume bounding); the f(ai)²r promise of "every interaction is observable" implies on. Sizing exercise: count GETs/day on MFFD-Dropbox, multiply by `retention-days=730`, check Neo4j page-cache + disk delta. If green, flip the default for `/v2/` paths only (v1 stays off to keep upstream-compat ops cost predictable). Pairs with PROV-RESOLVER-PATHWALK + PROV-V1-NUMERIC-LOOKUP — flipping reads without resolver fixes just multiplies the NULL-target row count. | S (design) + M (impl) | queued | Design call. Subsumes the f(ai)²r AI-collaboration provenance line in `aidocs/55 §4` and the RDM-004 Bucket A verdict. |
| RDM-002-E2E-FIX | **RDM-002 Playwright e2e fails on live despite code shipped + smoke green.** All 5 tests in `e2e/tests/rdm-002-orcid-on-profile.spec.ts` failed on `expect(getByTestId("profile-identity-section")).toBeVisible()` post-deploy `4ef13776`. Source has the test-id; `useRouteFragment` is hash-based and `/me#profile` matches `UserFragments.PROFILE`. Likely a race: spec asserts before the SSR-hydrated `routeFragment` ref updates. Add `await page.waitForSelector('[data-testid="profile-identity-section"]', { timeout: 5000 })` or `await page.waitForLoadState('networkidle')` before the assertion. | XS | queued | RDM-002 follow-up. Code is correct on live; test needs reliability hardening. |
| BUG-LJ-V1-COLL-ID | **`GET /v2/collections/{appId}/lab-journal-entries` returns 500 on any collection with entries** (LUMEN exposes it; MFFD-Dropbox hid it with empty list). Surfaced by RDM-005 widget agent 2026-05-24. **Brief's hypothesis was wrong by primary evidence**: not a v1-numeric-id → appId resolver gap — LUMEN's Collection node already has `appId=019e30b0-...` populated and `EntityIdResolver.resolveLong` succeeds; the resolver is irrelevant to this bug. **Actual root cause**: `CollectionLabJournalEntriesDAO`'s `RETURN DISTINCT lje` projection did not hydrate the INCOMING `has_labjournalentry` edge back to DataObject, so `LabJournalEntry.getDataObject()` came back null on every entry and `LabJournalEntryIO`'s constructor NPEd on `dataObject.getShepardId()`. **Fix**: DAO Cypher now projects a depth-1 neighbourhood path (`MATCH path=(lje)-[*0..1]-(n) ... RETURN lje, nodes(path), relationships(path)`) — the canonical `CypherQueryHelper.getReturnPart` pattern — so the OGM hydrates both directions. Resource adds a defensive orphan-skip + WARN log as belt-and-braces. Unrelated to PROV-V1-NUMERIC-LOOKUP. | S | ✅ **shipped** 2026-05-24 | See `aidocs/agent-findings/bug-lj-v1-coll-id-fix-2026-05-24.md`. Live verification post-deploy. |
| OGM-HYDRATION-AUDIT | **Audit every `findByQuery` callsite in v2 DAOs for the `RETURN <entity>`-only pattern that triggered BUG-LJ-V1-COLL-ID** — any place returning just the leaf node without a `nodes(path), relationships(path)` projection silently drops INCOMING relationships, and the bug only surfaces when the IO/service touches those fields. The canonical safe pattern is `CypherQueryHelper.getReturnPart(entity)`. Sweep should catch other UI-XXX bulk endpoints landed in 2026-05 that may carry the same defect (e.g., new collection-walk DAOs in `de.dlr.shepard.v2.*.daos`). | S | queued | Filed 2026-05-24 by BUG-LJ-V1-COLL-ID fix. Cheap audit; one-off grep + manual review of each hit. Prevents recurrence of the same class of bug in sister bulk endpoints. |
| MK-REDEPLOY-FORCE-RECREATE | **`make redeploy-frontend` ships stale image because `docker compose up -d --no-build` reuses the existing container even after `image-frontend` rebuilt.** Surfaced independently by Pattern-D agent + UX-bundle agent 2026-05-24. Recovery: `docker compose up -d --force-recreate frontend`. Fix: fold `--force-recreate frontend` (and the same for backend) into the Makefile `redeploy-frontend` + `redeploy-backend` targets. Authoritative live-deploy verify: `docker exec infrastructure-frontend-1 grep -l <new-testid> /app/server/chunks/build/*.mjs`. | XS | ✅ **shipped** 2026-05-24 | OPS hygiene bundle. `--force-recreate <service>` added to `redeploy-backend`, `redeploy-frontend`, `redeploy`, and `redeploy-fast`. See `aidocs/agent-findings/ops-hygiene-bundle-2026-05-24.md`. |
| E2E-AUTH-TOLERANT-LOGIN | **`loginAs` in `e2e/tests/helpers/auth.ts` times out ~30% when Keycloak SSO cookie is hot** — the Sign In button bounces back to `/` without showing the form. UX-bundle agent shipped a local `tolerantLogin` that handles both the cookie-hot and cookie-cold paths. Fold the pattern back into the shared helper so every spec benefits + the RDM-002-E2E-FIX flakiness disappears. | XS | ✅ **shipped** 2026-05-24 | OPS hygiene bundle. Shared `loginAs` now tolerates SSO-cookie-hot + cookie-cold + NextAuth redirect-loop. Five specs' local copies (`ux-polish-2026-05-24`, `rdm-001`, `rdm-002`, `rdm-005`, `ux-pattern-d-count-badges`) collapsed back to the shared helper. |
| CRIT-MAIN-BROKEN-TARGETENTITYRESOLVER-DUPLICATE | **`backend/src/main/java/de/dlr/shepard/provenance/filters/TargetEntityResolver.java` declares two `resolve(String path)` methods** — one instance (line 49), one static (line 85) — and `mvn clean compile` fails with `method resolve(java.lang.String) is already defined in class TargetEntityResolver`. Reproduced on `main @ 373543df` from a freshly-checked-out worktree (no dirty mods), so this is a real main-branch break, not local pollution. Surfaced by the CRIT-SMOKE-NOT-CATCHING-BUILD-BREAK self-test in the OPS hygiene bundle agent run — exactly the trap the fix is designed to catch (the smoke endpoint had been reporting 25/25 PASS against the stale running backend image while `mvn clean compile` was already red). Owner: provenance / PROV-RESOLVER-PATHWALK touch surface, likely landed during the PROV-2026-05-24 work. Fix shape (unverified): collapse the two `resolve` overloads or rename the static to `resolveStatic` / `parsePath`. | XS | queued | Filed 2026-05-24 by the OPS hygiene bundle agent. **Blocks every fresh-worktree backend build until fixed.** Operators running canonical `/opt/shepard` won't see it because their `target/` was built before the duplicate landed. |
| RDM-005a | **RDM-005 server-side completeness scoring + harvest filter + child-DO aggregate + embargo/funder checks.** Deferred from RDM-005 v0 (client-side only). Adds `GET /v2/collections/{appId}/completeness` so external harvesters (re3data, OpenAIRE, Helmholtz Databus) can filter by completeness score. Aggregate child-DO annotations into the Collection-level score (design call — would partially mask Collection-level gaps; alternative: separate "DO-level metadata health" rollup). Add embargo end-date check (needs the `embargo_until` field from LIC1's deferred slice). Add funder grant reference check (DataCite §17 FundingReference — needs a `funding[]` field). "Show only failing" filter on the widget's per-check list. | M | queued | RDM-005 deferred follow-up. |

## MONGO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-* — MongoDB substrate audit (live shepard)

Filed 2026-05-24 by the **MongoDB substrate audit agent** running against
live `infrastructure-mongodb-1` (MongoDB 8.0.4). Findings file:
`aidocs/agent-findings/mongodb-substrate-audit-2026-05-24.md`. Pairs with
sibling agent #209's file-routing investigation; both feed
`MFFD-DB-AUDIT-REAL-DATA`.

| ID | Description | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| MONGO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-001 | **N+1 in `StructuredDataSearchService.findMatchingReferences:76-95`** — one Mongo round-trip per reachable reference. Confirms long-standing SD1 backlog row with live evidence. Fix: either ship SD1 (deprecate Mongo SD query path → Postgres), or batch the per-container `find()` calls into a single `$or` / `$in` over the union of reachable containers. **MAJOR**. | M | queued | Cite to SD1. Audit row is the perf-evidence partner. |
| MONGO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-002 | **One Mongo collection per FileContainer + StructuredDataContainer** (`FileService.createFileContainer`, `StructuredDataService.createStructuredDataContainer`). Proven not to scale: BUG-F surfaced 4 197 SD collections at MFFD volume. Mongo-side cleanup ran post-redrive but **Neo4j carries 4 197 `:StructuredDataContainer{deleted: TRUE}` tombstones with no Mongo counterpart** (verified 2026-05-24 sample of 5 mongoIds: all GONE from Mongo). Long-term fix is structural (SD1 → Postgres for SD; FS1 family already in flight for files). Short-term fix: GC the Neo4j tombstones. **MAJOR**. | M | queued | Pairs with SD-WIPE-AND-REGET + SM1 retention. |
| MONGO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-003 | **JSON-string concatenation to build Mongo query** in `StructuredDataSearchService:91` (`mongoQuery += ", " + mongoSearchQuery + "}"` → `Document.parse(mongoQuery)`). Same shape as the C5/C5b Cypher string-build pattern that was explicitly killed in this fork. Should use `com.mongodb.client.model.Filters` DSL. Lower exploit ceiling than the Cypher case (Mongo `$where` is not used anywhere) but still wrong. **MAJOR**. | S | queued | Pairs with MONGO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-001 — both die when SD1 ships. |
| MONGO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-004 | **No backend-side array-wrap fallback in `StructuredDataService.createStructuredData:53`** (`Document.parse(payload.getPayload())`). BUG-E v15.12 wraps client-side in the importer; any non-importer client POSTing a JSON array as SD payload still 500s with the BSON-array exception. Defensive fix: detect `payload.trim().startsWith("[")` → wrap as `{items: [...], _wrapped: "v15.12-bug-e"}` server-side. Closes the BUG-E class permanently. **MAJOR**. | S | queued | Sibling: `MFFD-SD-BACKEND-WRAP-FALLBACK` (preexisting). |
| MONGO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-005 | **No `$jsonSchema` validators on any of 21 collections.** Cheap wins available on the singleton-schema collections: `userAvatars` (4 fields), `_shepard_files`, `_shepard_videos`, and the bookkeeping shape inside every `FileContainer*` (`{createdAt, name, md5, fileSize, FileMongoId}`). Per-container SD collections must stay polymorphic by design. Supports the FAIR R1 rigour the platform is reaching for. **MAJOR**. | S | queued | Pairs with FAIR-R1.x posture work. |
| MONGO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-006 | **`FileService.deleteFileContainer:237-240` sequential per-doc GridFS delete loop.** N round-trips to delete N files in a container. Bulk variants exist in driver 5.1+ (`bucket.delete(List<ObjectId>)`). For the canonical MFFD `FileContainer7693e977…` (34 files) this is 34 round-trips on every cleanup. **MINOR**. | XS | queued | Local fix; no design dep. |
| MONGO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-007 | **`FileMongoId` stored as STRING but `fs.files._id` is ObjectId** across `_shepard_files`, `_shepard_videos`, every `FileContainer*` collection. Java side casts at every read (`new ObjectId(...)`) so correctness holds, but any Mongo aggregation `$lookup` join from a shadow collection into `fs.files` silently returns empty unless the join expression pre-casts. Future analytics / cleanup / orphan-scan jobs will trip on this. Mitigations: (a) store as ObjectId; (b) document the convention loudly; (c) add a `$lookup`-with-`$convert` helper. **MINOR**. | S | queued | Migration would need V## Mongo data fix (every shadow collection). |
| MONGO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-008 | **`StructuredDataService.createStructuredData:60-61` silently strips underscore-prefixed user keys.** `var forbidden = toInsert.keySet().stream().filter(k -> k.startsWith("_")).toList(); forbidden.forEach(toInsert::remove);` — user payload `_my_field` is data-lost without warning. Should: (a) log a `Log.warn` on every strip; (b) restrict to known-conflicting keys (`_id`, `_meta`) instead of all `_*`; (c) reject the payload with 400 + field-list if any conflict. **MINOR**. | XS | queued | Cheap fix; the silent-data-loss class is the worst kind of API foot-gun. |
| MONGO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-009 | **No Mongo connection-pool config.** Driver defaults apply (`maxPoolSize=100`, `minPoolSize=0`, `maxIdleTimeMS=∞`, `serverSelectionTimeoutMS=30s`). Document defaults explicitly in `application.properties` + tune from Prometheus metrics per PERF2b's `mongo_latency_high` rule. **GAP**. | S | queued | Cite PERF2b. |
| MONGO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-010 | **No TTL indexes anywhere.** Nothing self-prunes. SM1 retention and PRE-MUT-SNAP* both need this; today their snapshots / orphan-grace data would grow without bound in Mongo. Audit row is the dependency-flag for those two designs. **GAP**. | M | queued | Cite SM1 + PRE-MUT-SNAP1. |
| MONGO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-011 | **`quarkus.mongodb.connection-string=mongodb://mongo@mongodb:27017` carries no DB name; `MongoClientWrapper.init()` silently falls back to literal `"database"`.** An admin who overrides the URI and forgets the DB segment lands writes into the wrong DB without error. Fix: log loudly at startup, or refuse start when DB name absent (the prod URI already has it; this would only affect future overrides). **GAP**. | XS | queued | One-liner: throw on missing DB name. |
| MONGO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-012 | **No per-collection / per-container Mongo size cap.** A single 532 MB `Confluence-space-export-151906-2.html.zip` upload (2026-05-22) is 60% of the entire Mongo substrate. Add: (a) admin alert when any container exceeds `shepard.mongo.container.max-bytes` (default 1 GiB); (b) `shepard.mongo.file.max-bytes` upload-rejection cap (default 2 GiB). Pair with SM1a's 1-year default retention. **GAP**. | S | queued | Cite SM1a. |
| MONGO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-013 | **3× duplicate `lumen-hotfire.mp4` blobs in `_shepard_videos`** (8.6 MB each × 3 = 26 MB redundant). Same MD5, distinct ObjectIds — each upload created a fresh GridFS blob with no dedup. Stop-gap: deduplicate by MD5 + reuse the existing blob if present. Long-term: SHA-256-content-addressable storage is the FS1/Garage trajectory, but the GridFS path inherits the dup-tolerant behaviour today. **MINOR**. | S | queued | Cosmetic at current scale; structural at MFFD scale. |
| MONGO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-014 | **6 empty per-container Mongo collections (24 KB wasted) — `StructuredDataContainer839614f2`, `…54ec30b6`, `…4702ed7d`, `…4786abf3`, `…6931e4d4`, `…4277ad7c`, `FileContainerecc172da`, `FileContainer8a3e519e`.** Each is a placeholder that was created but never written to. Either the container-create endpoint doesn't roll back on subsequent failure, or the data shape permits create-and-never-use. Investigate the create path for missing transactional bookkeeping. **MINOR**. | XS | queued | Audit-trail-followup. |
