| PLUGIN-HDF5-AUDIT-2026-05-24-003 | **Garage storage backend flip — HSDS `HSDS_AWS_S3_GATEWAY=http://garage:3900`.** Zero app-code change; one env-var change on the HSDS sidecar. Gated on `garage-and-docker-stack-audit-2026-05-24.md` Garage GA per ADR-0024. | XS | gated-on-garage | Audit §HDF5.C. |
| PLUGIN-HDF5-AUDIT-2026-05-24-004 | **A5c unblock — `HdfReference` per-DataObject anchor at dataset path.** Already queued as A5c; this row is a redundant pointer for plugin-audit traceability. Add Neo4j `CREATE INDEX FOR (n:HdfReference) ON (n.datasetPath)` to the migration when shipping. | S | queued | Audit §HDF5.C + existing row A5c. |
| PLUGIN-HDF5-AUDIT-2026-05-24-005 | **A5e unblock — h5pyd token bridge (`/api-keys/{id}/hsds-token`).** Already queued as A5e; redundant pointer. Unblocks the canonical h5pyd ergonomics deliverable per `aidocs/35 §1`. | S-M | queued | Audit §HDF5.G + existing row A5e. |

### Cross-cutting (apply to all 3 + future plugins)

| ID | Item | effort | status | notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| PM1f-MIGRATION-SPATIAL-HDF5-2026-05-24 | **PM1f sweep — declare sidecars in spatial + hdf5 manifests; remove `postgis` + `shepard-hsds` from central `infrastructure/docker-compose.yml`.** Bundle PLUGIN-SPATIAL-AUDIT-2026-05-24-001 + PLUGIN-HDF5-AUDIT-2026-05-24-001 into one PR; pattern: deploy automation reads plugin manifests and re-emits compose. Cross-ref existing `FileS3PluginManifestSidecarsTest` for test pattern. | S | queued | Cross-cutting finding §1. Headline gap of this audit. |
| PLUGIN-MANIFEST-TEST-BASECLASS-2026-05-24 | **Introduce `AbstractPluginManifestTest<T extends PluginManifest>` base class** asserting `id()` / `version()` / `shepardCompatibility()` / `sidecars()` shape. Every plugin manifest test extends it. Today only `file-s3` has manifest + sidecar tests; spatial + hdf5 + aas + git + kip + minter-* + video + unhide all skip the pattern. Enforces consistency. | S | queued | Cross-cutting finding §4. |
| SPI-FRONTEND-CONTRIBUTION-2026-05-24 | **Design `FrontendContribution` SPI** — let plugins ship a frontend bundle (Vue SFC + manifest declaring "this kind needs a viewer component"); shepard frontend dynamic-imports. Today all three plugins (spatial / hdf5 / tables-future) need a hand-coded sibling in the main `frontend/` tree, which couples plugin frontends to the core release cadence. Out-of-scope for the plugin audit itself; file as a design dispatch. | M (design) | queued | Cross-cutting finding §5. |
| POSTGRES-MULTITENANT-SCHEMA-DECISION | **Decide: collapse multiple Postgres instances (TS-Postgres + postgis) into one with multiple schemas + extensions.** Three plugins want PG (TS, Tables, Spatial); current shape has two PG instances and is heading for three. Right answer: one PG + schemas `shepard_ts` (TimescaleDB hypertable) + `shepard_spatial` (PostGIS GIST) + `shepard_tables` (typed row data). Win: real SQL JOINs across substrates + simpler ops + one PgBouncer pool tree. Loss: less isolation; mitigation via PgBouncer per-schema pool. Gated on the in-flight `pgbouncer-audit` pool-sizing answer. | M (decision) + L (impl if chosen) | queued | Cross-cutting finding §3. Covers PLUGIN-SPATIAL-AUDIT-2026-05-24-004 + PLUGIN-TABLES-AUDIT-2026-05-24-004 with one decision. |

## TS-AUDIT-2026-05-24-* — TimescaleDB design audit findings

Source: [`aidocs/agent-findings/ts-design-audit-2026-05-24.md`](agent-findings/ts-design-audit-2026-05-24.md). Substrate-direct read-only audit of the live TimescaleDB 2.24.0 / PG16 instance on 2026-05-24. **Verdict: MIXED** — 12 findings (2 CRITICAL, 5 MAJOR, 5 MINOR/observe). Operator's "very badly designed" hypothesis is REFUTED for the lifecycle/index/compression layer (V1.4/V1.7/V1.8/V1.11 migrations are thoughtful; 23× compression ratio achieved; chunk_skipping enabled) but CONFIRMED for the write-path (string-INSERT per batch) and the value-storage shape (4-column polymorphism).

| ID | Item | effort | status | notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| TS-AUDIT-2026-05-24-001 | **CRITICAL (latent) — 4-column polymorphic value table.** `timeseries_data_points` carries `double_value`, `int_value`, `string_value`, `boolean_value`; 100% of 81M live rows are Double; 3 columns × 81M rows ≈ 2 GB dead weight. No `CHECK` constraint enforces exactly-one-non-null. Compounds once Boolean/String containers land (expected for MFFD welding digital IO + state machines). Cheap fix: `CHECK (num_nonnulls(...) = 1)` constraint (paired with TS-AUDIT-2026-05-24-003). Proper fix: defer to the TS-ID migration (`aidocs/platform/87`) — partition by value-type into N hypertables, OR collapse to a single typed column. | XS (constraint) / L (column-drop) | queued | Audit AP-1. References TimescaleDB schema-design docs + Pavlo CMU 15-445 lecture 5. Pair with -003. |
| TS-AUDIT-2026-05-24-002 | **CRITICAL (write path) — `INSERT…VALUES (…) ON CONFLICT DO UPDATE` builds fresh SQL per batch.** `TimeseriesDataPointRepository.buildInsertQueryObject` (line 207) constructs a unique SQL string with up to 20 001 placeholders per batch; `prepareThreshold=0` (required for PgBouncer transaction-mode) defeats the JDBC statement cache → every batch pays full parse + plan. **The COPY-based `insertManyDataPointsWithCopyCommand` already exists in the same file** (line 81) but only the Influx migration uses it. Route live writes through COPY for batches > 1000 rows; keep the parametric path for small batches. Conflict-handling preserved via session-scoped TEMP TABLE + dedupe-then-COPY. | M | queued | Audit AP-2. References TimescaleDB write-path best practice. Highest-leverage single fix in the audit. |
| TS-AUDIT-2026-05-24-003 | **MAJOR — no `CHECK` constraint pairing value columns to `timeseries.value_type`.** The `timeseries` table guards its own `value_type` enum but `timeseries_data_points` has zero constraints linking rows to their parent's declared type. A misbehaving writer could insert `string_value` on a Double series and the DAO `getColumnName(valueType)` switch would never read it. Today only the DAO writes; the upcoming plugin SPI (Influx-line-protocol shim, OPC-UA bridge) breaks the assumption. Add `ALTER TABLE timeseries_data_points ADD CONSTRAINT chk_one_value_column CHECK (num_nonnulls(double_value, int_value, string_value, boolean_value) = 1);` — cheap, idempotent. | XS | queued | Audit AP-3. Pair with -001. |
| TS-AUDIT-2026-05-24-004 | **MAJOR (at scale) — FK from hypertable to `timeseries` metadata.** `timeseries_data_points.timeseries_id → timeseries(id) ON DELETE CASCADE` is propagated to all 29 chunks (30 FK constraints visible in `pg_constraint`). Every INSERT triggers a lookup — visible as 600K+ `timeseries_unique_b4a836fabc25` scans. Industry pattern: avoid FK on hypertables at high ingest; rely on application-level integrity + periodic GC sweep. Add `shepard.timeseries.fk.enabled` runtime flag (default true); idempotent drop-and-recreate migration; pairs with SM1a retention sweep. | S | queued | Audit AP-4. References TimescaleDB FK FAQ. Only matters above ~10K inserts/s; today the load is 87/s peak. |
| TS-AUDIT-2026-05-24-005 | **MAJOR (observability blind spot) — no `pg_stat_statements` extension.** Zero query-shape observability today; this audit had to read code instead of metrics. One-line `shared_preload_libraries='timescaledb,pg_stat_statements'` config + Flyway `V1.12.0__add_pg_stat_statements.sql` (CREATE EXTENSION). TimescaleDB tuning guide recommends it for every production instance. Free win. | XS | queued | Audit AP-5. Single highest cost-to-value gap in the audit. |
| TS-AUDIT-2026-05-24-006 | **MAJOR — no continuous aggregates for chart-view bucketed reads.** `TimeseriesContainerChartViewService` runs `time_bucket()` / `time_bucket_gapfill()` against the raw hypertable on every render. Invisible on demo data (0.4ms reads) but compounds at MFFD-scale (multi-million-row series × hundreds-of-buckets × multiple channels per chart). Ship one CA per canonical bucket (1m, 5m, 1h, 1d) `WITH (materialized_only = false)` so newer data falls through to raw rows; wire Chart View service to pick the matching bucket. | M | queued | Audit AP-6. References TimescaleDB CA docs. |
| TS-AUDIT-2026-05-24-007 | **MAJOR (or deliberate) — no data retention policy on `timeseries_data_points`.** Only `Job History Log Retention Policy` exists; data points grow forever. Memory (`project_storage_management.md`, `feedback_referenced_data_infinite_retention.md`) implies "referenced=infinite-grace, orphans=SM1a retention", which means TS should still have an SM1a-driven sweep at the container level — currently nothing fires. Either document the "no retention by design" call in `aidocs/data/00-model-inventory.md` or add a generous `add_retention_policy('timeseries_data_points', INTERVAL '10 years')` safety net. Aligns with SM1a. | S (decision) + S (impl if chosen) | queued | Audit AP-7. Cross-references SM1a. |
| TS-AUDIT-2026-05-24-008 | **MAJOR (operational) — backfill creates uncompressed chunks the policy won't sweep for ≤24h.** Example from today: chunk 51 (Jan 2023 data) created at 12:26, compression job last ran 11:56, next run tomorrow 11:57. 1 GB uncompressed chunk sits for 23h+. MFFD ingest currently creates these at multiple-per-hour cadence → temporary disk inflation 5-10×. Add `TimeseriesDataPointRepository.compressBackfilledChunks()` that compresses any chunk older than 8 days not already compressed; call from importer post-import phase + as a fortnightly maintenance job. | S | queued | Audit AP-8. Hooks into v15.x importer's existing post-phase. |
| TS-AUDIT-2026-05-24-009 | **MAJOR (already-designed) — 5-tuple lookup planning cost.** Measured: 1.65ms planning vs 0.095ms execution. Per-channel lookups in the hot path pay 17× the actual work in parse + plan. Fix is known: TS-ID migration per `aidocs/platform/87` (`shepard_id` UUID single-column lookup, V1.11 substrate already in place). This row is a cross-reference + audit confirmation that the design's load-shape evidence is real. | (sized in aidocs/87) | queued | Audit AP-9. Cross-ref `aidocs/platform/87`. |
| TS-AUDIT-2026-05-24-010 | **MINOR (observe, do not fix) — three indexes per chunk with partly overlapping shapes.** UNIQUE `(timeseries_id, time)` ASC + `(timeseries_id, time DESC)` + `(time DESC)`. The DESC variant was added deliberately by V1.8 with documented rationale + the empirical scan counts justify it (14K-44K scans/chunk for the DESC vs 21M for the UNIQUE). If write-amp becomes a concern at MFFD-scale, the DESC variant is the first drop candidate — but only after measuring with pg_stat_statements (TS-AUDIT-005). | (observe) | parked | Audit AP-10. Not a fix; a calibration note for future perf work. |
| TS-AUDIT-2026-05-24-011 | **MINOR — unbounded INSERT batch parameter count vs Postgres wire-protocol limit.** `INSERT_BATCH_SIZE=20000` × ~2 params/row ≈ 20 002 placeholders/query (1 fixed `:timeseriesid` + 2 per row); Postgres `Bind` message uses `int16` for parameter count (max 32 767). Today: under the limit. Risk: any tweak that doubles the batch size hits the wall. Add `assert (effectiveParameterCount < 32767)` guard at batch construction; or (better) the COPY migration in -002 makes this irrelevant. | XS | queued | Audit AP-11. Pairs with -002 (COPY has no such limit). |
| TS-AUDIT-2026-05-24-012 | **MINOR (research-data concern) — no row-level provenance / write origin on hypertable rows.** Every other entity in shepard carries `:Activity`-shaped provenance per the f(ai)²r differentiator (`project_fair2r_integration.md`); TS data points do not. Adding per-row `inserted_at` / `inserted_by` would negate the compression ratio. **Cheaper shape**: add `source_run_id BIGINT` (NULL default) FKing the existing `importer_run` table. Backfilled rows carry the run id; live MQTT writes stay NULL (observable via collector). Storage cost ~zero (single NULL bitmap bit when unused). | S | queued | Audit AP-12. Architectural tension with compression; only worth doing once research-data audit pressure asks for it. |

## NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-* — Neo4j + n10s substrate audit (findings)

Source: `aidocs/agent-findings/neo4j-n10s-design-audit-2026-05-24.md` (sibling
of the TimescaleDB / file-storage / Mongo / Postgres / Docker stack audits).
3 CRITICAL + 6 MAJOR + 4 MINOR antipatterns; 3 best-practice gaps. Read the
findings doc first — every row below carries `EVIDENCE: ` Cypher and a
`RECOMMENDATION` referencing primary docs.

| ID | Item | effort | status | notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-001 | **CRITICAL — `:Activity` nodes are provenance write-only, not graph-queryable.** 284,530 Activity nodes exist with **ZERO incoming or outgoing edges**. `Activity.java:21-23` documents `(:User)-[:WAS_ASSOCIATED_WITH]->(:Activity)` + `:USED` / `:GENERATED` edges as "not yet wired in this slice" — they were never wired. Only 0.05 % (144 of 284,535) Activity rows carry a `targetAppId` property; no index on it. Result: "what activities touched DataObject X" needs a 569,069-dbHit full-label scan. The f(ai)²r promise of every-interaction-observable is not actually observable from the graph today. **Fix:** wire the three PROV-O edges in `ProvenanceCaptureFilter` write path + backfill migration on 284k existing rows (parse `Activity.path` via `TargetEntityResolver`, read `Activity.agentUsername`). Sequence **after** `PROV-RESOLVER-PATHWALK` so the resolver is the single shared source. Citation: W3C PROV-O `wasAssociatedWith` https://www.w3.org/TR/prov-o/#wasAssociatedWith. | M | queued | Audit NEO-001. Sibling of PROV-RESOLVER-PATHWALK + PROV-V1-NUMERIC-LOOKUP. **Highest impact** of the audit's findings. |
| NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-002 | **CRITICAL — `:ShepardFile.providerId` populated on 0.6 % of rows** (11,834 NULL / 71 gridfs / 33 s3 of 11,902 total). V34 backfill missed the legacy population; every reader must keep the `NULL → gridfs` fallback baked in. File-storage routing audit (sibling) lands on the same gap from the read side. **Fix:** one-shot Cypher backfill `MATCH (sf:ShepardFile) WHERE sf.providerId IS NULL SET sf.providerId = 'gridfs'` + write-path `@Required` on the entity + reader-side NULL-coalesce drop in a follow-up PR. | XS | queued | Audit NEO-002. Sibling cross-substrate finding (file-storage routing audit #209). |
| NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-003 | **CRITICAL — all 596 `:Timeseries.appId` rows are NULL** despite the `appId_unique_Timeseries` constraint existing — uniqueness constraints permit NULL, so it's satisfied but useless. The schema layer is already provisioned (constraint + range index in place); only the data layer is empty. **Fix:** the L2c-shaped TS-appId migration in `aidocs/platform/87-timeseries-appid-migration.md` — mint UUID-v7 appIds for every existing Timeseries node, populate, then deprecate the 5-tuple as identity. Per `feedback_appid_to_shepardid.md` the field gets renamed to `shepardId` in the same pass. Audit observation: this migration is **closer to ready than the design doc implies** because the constraint + index already exist. | M | queued | Audit NEO-003. Pairs with TimescaleDB audit's 5-tuple finding. |
| NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-004 | **MAJOR — operator-`User` is a confirmed supernode (33,368 incoming edges).** The 2026-05-23 antipattern audit suspected this at MFFD scale and flagged it as "inconclusive"; MFFD ingest landed → confirmed. PROFILE of a `created_by` traversal through the operator User node takes 66,794 dbHits to walk 17,086 DataObjects. NEO-001 will worsen this once Activity edges land. **Fix (don't dump the supernode — it's structural):** add a time-bucketed Agent index `(:User)-[:created_in_month {ym:"202605"}]->(:DataObject)` written by the same hook that creates `created_by`. The MATCH plan becomes a label-scan on the `:created_in_month` rel with a `ym` predicate — typically 100-1000x reduction. Citation: Neo4j supernode KB https://neo4j.com/developer/kb/understanding-the-design-of-supernodes/. | S | queued | Audit NEO-004. Pre-emptive — bounded today, trajectory points to 100k+ edges within a year. |
| NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-005 | **MAJOR — EAV-on-graph: 90+ distinct `attributes||*` keys on `:DataObject`.** MFFD real-data ingest flooded the schema with single-use attribute keys (`attributes||hypothesis` × 1, `attributes||defect_area_cm2` × 1, …). The Neo4j-OGM `@Properties` flatten on `AbstractDataObject.attributes:Map<String,String>` creates one Neo4j property per map key on every node — the graph DB analogue of EAV. Quantifies §1.1.A of the 2026-05-23 archived audit on real ingested data. **Specific harms post-MFFD:** `attributes||v16_pass1` × 8,507 is a transient ingest marker; `attributes||source_*` keys are import provenance (should be Activity properties, not DataObject); `attributes||license` × 3 coexists with the typed `license` field × 4 (LIC1 just shipped) — same semantic carried by two different fields. **Fix:** the SHACL-as-source-of-truth direction (`feedback_shacl_single_source_of_truth.md`) is the structural fix. Tactical: promote import provenance from `:DataObject.attributes||` to the `:Activity` node that recorded the import (pairs naturally with NEO-001). Drop `attributes||license` once LIC1 readers settle. | M | queued | Audit NEO-005. Pairs with NEO-001 + SHACL-as-SoT direction. |
| NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-006 | **MAJOR — mixed-case relationship-type convention.** Three shepard-side rels use UPPERCASE literals instead of the lowercase `Constants.*` convention: `ENTRY_OF` (`SnapshotEntry.java:59`), `SNAPSHOT_OF` (`Snapshot.java:82`), `OWNS_CREDENTIAL` (`User.java:79`). (All other UPPERCASE rels — `TYPE/SUBJECT/OBJECT/RELATED/BROADER/NARROWER/SUBCLASSOF/MIGRATED_TO/…` — are n10s/RDF-owned, upstream-mandated and stay uppercase.) Mixed-case convention drift is a long-tail bug source: `:has_successor` vs `:HAS_SUCCESSOR` would be silently distinct labels. **Fix:** rename to `entry_of`, `snapshot_of`, `owns_credential` in a Cypher migration (depends on APOC — see NEO-013 — or use the manual `MATCH-CREATE-DELETE` fallback). Coordinate with the appId→shepardId entity rename pass per `feedback_appid_to_shepardid.md`. | S | queued | Audit NEO-006. APOC dependency — schedule after NEO-013. |
| NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-007 | **MAJOR — duplicate Collection names with shared semantic (MFFD-Dropbox × 4).** Two of the four MFFD-Dropbox collections are supernodes themselves (8538 + 8518 edges). Per memory (`project_mffd_import_workflow.md`) this is intentional iterative ingest, NOT a bug — but operator-facing impact is real: `GET /v2/collections?name=MFFD-Dropbox` returns four hits and the UI can't tell which is which. **Fix:** no schema change. Add `:Collection.importedFrom: text` distinguishing the four (e.g., `tapelaying`, `bridgewelding`, `v15-redrive-1`, `v15-redrive-2`); surface on the collection list UI as a sub-label. Closes the human-identity ambiguity without merging graph nodes. | S | queued | Audit NEO-007. UI affordance + schema additive — no migration shape concerns. |
| NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-008 | **MAJOR — Cartesian OPTIONAL MATCH on `DataObjectDAO.java:480-506` + `CollectionDAO.java:120-121`.** Single super-node `:DataObject` Tapelaying-2026-05-23 carries 1470 `has_reference` edges; PROFILE shows 8840 dbHits for an empty result because the planner walks all 1470 refs in each leg. Sibling `OPTIONAL MATCH` legs against TimeseriesReference / FileBundleReference / StructuredDataReference multiply leg cardinalities. Quantifies §1.1.E of the 2026-05-23 archived audit on the largest MFFD DO. **Fix:** split sibling legs into `CALL { ... }` subqueries (Neo4j 4.4+) per the official cypher anti-patterns guide https://neo4j.com/developer-blog/cypher-anti-patterns-merge/. Expected reduction: 5-10x dbHits. | S | queued | Audit NEO-008. Same family as `BUG-LJ-V1-COLL-ID` + `OGM-HYDRATION-AUDIT`. |
| NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-009 | **MAJOR — `idx_Subscription_requestMethod` is the #3 hottest index in the system (298,700 reads) against zero rows.** Every authenticated write hits `SubscriptionService.findMatchingSubscriptions`, which probes the registry for matching watchers; the registry has zero `:Subscription` nodes so every probe is a wasted index walk. Also signals a feature-adoption gap — Subscription is shipped but unused; might indicate a creation bug. **Fix (two layers):** (a) short-circuit `findMatchingSubscriptions` with a cached `count(:Subscription) == 0` check (refreshed on subscription create/delete); when zero, skip the index lookup entirely. (b) file a separate adoption-audit task for the subscription feature. | XS + S | queued | Audit NEO-009. Cheap perf-win + a smell worth its own follow-up. |
| NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-010 | **MAJOR — duplicate user emails: 2× `alice@demo.shepard.local`, 2× `admin@demo.shepard.local`.** `unique_username_User` covers UUID usernames; no email uniqueness. Today dev-only, but a routine OIDC-as-email failure mode in production (shared department mailbox; two employees sharing an email). **Fix:** add `CREATE CONSTRAINT user_email_unique IF NOT EXISTS FOR (u:User) REQUIRE u.email IS UNIQUE` + one-shot reconciliation migration to merge the two `admin@`/`alice@` accounts. Graph-edge-relabel well-known shape; coordinate with the auth team. | S | queued | Audit NEO-010. |
| NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-011 | **MINOR — 47 indexes with zero reads (dead-index maintenance cost on every write).** Notable: `idx_Timeseries_attr_field`, `_location`, `_symbolic_name` TEXT indexes (V8) are unused — `device` + `measurement` are queried, the other three never (`lastRead=NULL`). 23 zero-read `appId_unique_*` constraints for entity types not in production use. Write-amplification at MFFD ingest: 33k writes × 47 indexes × 1ms ≈ 25 minutes of pure index-update CPU per ingest. **Fix:** drop the three unused Timeseries TEXT indexes + the Watch family if Watch is deprecated. **Don't** blanket-drop unique constraints — load-bearing for entity types even if not currently queried. | S | queued | Audit NEO-011. Cheap with measurable write-cost win at MFFD scale. |
| NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-012 | **MINOR — vestigial `unique_id_*` constraints on entities migrated to `appId`.** 100 % of DataObject / Collection / StructuredDataContainer rows have `id IS NULL` because the system migrated to `appId` as canonical identity; the 14 V1-era `unique_id_*` constraints still exist and protect a property that's never populated. No correctness risk (unique-on-NULL satisfied) — just contributor confusion. **Fix:** schedule a deprecation pass after L2e (the planned v1-numeric-id sunset, `aidocs/platform/25 §L2e`). Drop the 14 constraints once L2e ships and no readers depend on the property. | XS | queued | Audit NEO-012. Wait for L2e. |
| NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-013 | **MINOR — APOC absent on this instance despite security allowlist suggesting it should be present.** Container env: `NEO4J_PLUGINS=["n10s"]` but `NEO4J_dbms_security_procedures_allowlist=apoc.*,n10s.*` + `unrestricted=apoc.*,n10s.*`. The allowlist is correct; only the plugins list missed APOC. APOC core has been bundled with Neo4j 5.x since 5.7 (https://neo4j.com/labs/apoc/5/installation/) — no separate jar download needed. Blocks the rel-type rename in NEO-006 from using `apoc.refactor.setType`. **Fix:** one-line compose edit `NEO4J_PLUGINS=["apoc","n10s"]` + container restart. | XS | queued | Audit NEO-013. **Unblocks NEO-006** + future migrations needing `apoc.periodic.iterate`. |
| NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-014 | **MINOR — migration chain applied in non-monotonic order (V63 before V61).** Same incident as OPS-MIGRATION-HEALTHCHECK (V61 lagged main by two days). Correctness OK — the `Migrations` library applies forward-only on each restart — but a documentation foot-gun: readers of `MATCH (m) ORDER BY m.version DESC` see "63 happened 2026-05-22T15:38, 61 happened 2026-05-22T15:39+1day" and reasonably ask "was the order reversed?". **Fix:** add a comment to the existing OPS-MIGRATION-HEALTHCHECK runbook (`docs/admin/runbooks/migration-chain-integrity.md`) explaining the chain may carry out-of-order `installedOn` timestamps if a forward-only splice runs late, and that's WAI. | XS | queued | Audit NEO-014. Doc-only follow-up. |
| NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-015 | **MINOR — `:Activity.actionKind` is stringly-typed (3 distinct values, no enforcement).** Activity.java:50-51 documents an enum (`CREATE/READ/UPDATE/DELETE/EXECUTE`); stored as free-text. Today clean (`CREATE: 253520, UPDATE: 18050, DELETE: 12917`); single typo in capture filter forks the value-space and breaks downstream filters silently. Same shape as `:DataObject.status`, `:ImportPlan.status` from the 2026-05-23 audit. **Fix:** Neo4j 5 EE property-existence + value constraints (`REQUIRE n.actionKind IS IN [...]`) but this instance runs Community Edition (`NEO4J_EDITION=community`). Fallback: validation in `ProvenanceCaptureFilter` + periodic sweep alarm that fires if any `:Activity.actionKind` matches none of the canonical values. Lower-priority than NEO-001 — wire the edges first. | S | queued | Audit NEO-015. EE upgrade or app-layer validation. |
| NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-016 | **MINOR (best-practice gap) — soft-delete heavy on `:DataObject` (50 %) + `:BasicReference` (36 %) without TTL.** Half of all DataObjects soft-deleted; index walks always touch both populations. Coupled with NEO-004's supernode, "list DataObjects this user created (not deleted)" becomes O(33k × 2). **Fix:** SM1a (already in backlog, queued) — retention sweep hard-deletes soft-deleted DataObjects past a TTL. Pair naturally with this finding; just nudge SM1a priority up. | — | depends-on-SM1a | Audit NEO-016. No new effort — pre-existing backlog row. |
| NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-017 | **MINOR (best-practice gap) — property keys with single-row usage (sparse property store).** 30+ `attributes||*` keys appear on 1-3 DataObjects each. Neo4j's property store is record-oriented (not column-oriented) — a node with 30 properties takes 30 record reads even if your query reads one. Compounds NEO-005. **Fix:** same as NEO-005 — promote import-provenance attributes to Activity edges. Routine domain attributes stay pending SHACL-as-SoT. | — | depends-on-NEO-005 | Audit NEO-017. No standalone work. |
| NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-018 | **MINOR (best-practice gap) — 174,035 bare `:Resource` nodes (n10s SKOS import bloat).** NASA thesaurus + synaptica notes dominate (`BROADER:17012, NARROWER:17012, RELATED:117340`). Correct per n10s semantics (every RDF subject → `:Resource`) but ~2.4× shepard's domain node count. `n10s_unique_uri` is the #1 hottest index (26M reads) on these nodes; page cache stays warm with RDF infrastructure, possibly at the expense of hot DataObject reads. **Fix:** consider importing heavy SKOS thesauri with `n10s.skos.import.fetch` + `handleMultival="ARRAY"` + label-density reduction (omit `skos:related` if not used). Or sidecar to a separate substrate (Community single-DB limitation argues against). Lower priority — copes today. | M | queued | Audit NEO-018. Pairs with `aidocs/semantics/14` semantic-improvements design. |

## Synthesis Pass-1 cheap-wins — shipped 2026-05-24

Tracking the synthesis report's §6 Pass-1 trio + the newly proposed
CADDY row. Bundled here because they were chosen as the MFFD-orthogonal
work pack while ingest still runs (none touch the destination data).

| ID | Item | effort | status | notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-002-SHIPPED | **Cypher backfill `MATCH (sf:ShepardFile) WHERE sf.providerId IS NULL SET sf.providerId = 'gridfs'`.** Closed the substrate side of NEO-002. Pre-state: 12 253 NULL + 71 gridfs + 33 s3. Post-state: 12 327 gridfs + 33 s3 + 0 NULL (12 256 rows updated; +3 drift from ingest during the backfill itself). Reader-side NULL-coalesce stays in place until the write-path `@Required` annotation lands as a follow-up; backfill remains idempotent so it can be re-run if MFFD ingest creates a few more NULL rows before that PR. **Did not** touch any MFFD destination data — `:ShepardFile` is instance-wide. | XS | ✅ shipped 2026-05-24 | Commit landing this row. Follow-up: write-path `@Required` + reader NULL-coalesce drop, sequenced after MFFD ingest drains. |
| CADDY-API-PASSTHROUGH-2026-05-24 | **Caddy `/v2/*` + `/shepard/api/*` + `/shepard/doc/*` bypass routes to backend:8080.** Closes Digital Native persona §0: programmatic callers arriving at `https://shepard.nuclide.systems/` with `X-API-KEY` / `Bearer` used to land at the Nuxt frontend (302→NextAuth signin). Verified end-to-end via Zoraxy: `https://shepard.nuclide.systems/v2/collections` now returns HTTP/2 401 with `content-type: application/json` (backend challenge) instead of 302→signin; `https://shepard.nuclide.systems/shepard/doc/openapi/v2.json` serves the spec. The Nuxt frontend uses `NUXT_PUBLIC_BACKEND_API_URL=https://shepard-api.nuclide.systems/shepard/api` for its own calls so no SSR breakage; only `/api/auth/*` lives same-origin in Nuxt and is preserved. New helper doc `docs/help/api-access.md` covers API-key minting, OpenAPI client generation, MCP from Claude, common failure modes. **Caddy bind-mount gotcha:** Caddy's `caddy reload` did NOT pick up the new Caddyfile because Write tool's atomic rename changed the inode and single-file bind mounts in Docker track the inode at container-start time. Fix: `docker compose restart caddy` (brief gateway downtime, ~3s). Memory entry filed. | S | ✅ shipped 2026-05-24 | Commit landing this row. New row — not present in any source audit (synthesis §3-T3 + §5#6 flagged "newly proposed"). |
| NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-013-DEFERRED | **APOC plugin install (`NEO4J_PLUGINS=["apoc","n10s"]` + container restart).** Synthesis §6 Pass-1 candidate — moved here because the Neo4j restart it requires would interrupt the active MFFD ingest. Promote to ✅ when ingest drains. | XS | gated-on-ingest-pause | Re-pickup when MFFD ingest signals done. |
| TS-AUDIT-2026-05-24-005-DEFERRED | **`pg_stat_statements` extension + Flyway V1.12 migration.** Synthesis §6 Pass-1 candidate — moved here because the `shared_preload_libraries` change requires Postgres restart, which would interrupt MFFD TS writes. Promote to ✅ when ingest drains. | XS | gated-on-ingest-pause | Re-pickup when MFFD ingest signals done. |
| LIM-DOCKER-BIND-MOUNT-INODE | **Single-file Docker bind mounts track inode-at-mount-time, not path-at-runtime.** Surfaced 2026-05-24 by CADDY-API-PASSTHROUGH: editing the host file via Claude's Write tool (atomic temp-file + rename) changes the inode, so the container view goes stale and Caddy reloads see the old file. The fix is `docker compose restart <service>` (or use `docker cp` to overwrite in-place). Affected files in this repo: `infrastructure/proxy/Caddyfile`, `infrastructure/.env`. **Operator runbook follow-up:** add a one-page note to `docs/admin/runbooks/` and a guard rail in the OPS hygiene set (smoke probe should detect "container file does not match host file"). | XS | queued | Operator-facing follow-up. Filed by CADDY-API-PASSTHROUGH-2026-05-24. |

## OGM-HYDRATE-2026-05-24-* — v2 DAO hydration sweep (4 rows from audit)

SSOT: [`aidocs/agent-findings/ogm-hydration-audit-2026-05-24.md`](agent-findings/ogm-hydration-audit-2026-05-24.md). Sweep ran 2026-05-24; **zero CRIT v2 findings** (v2 is accidentally inoculated — flat property bags with appId references, no `@Relationship` fields). One v1 DEFERRED + one v2 DEFERRED + two structural follow-ups.

| ID | Item | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| OGM-HYDRATE-2026-05-24-001 | **OGM-HYDRATE-V1-001** — `backend/.../context/labJournal/daos/LabJournalEntryRevisionDAO.java:32-41`. `LabJournalEntryRevision` carries `@Relationship(direction=INCOMING) LabJournalEntry`. DAO `RETURN DISTINCT revision` will NPE the moment a `LabJournalEntryRevisionIO` ships that reads `revision.getLabJournalEntry().getShepardId()`. Same defect class as the just-shipped BUG-LJ-V1-COLL-ID fix. **Trigger condition**: any new IO serialisation referencing the entry's back-reference. Fix shape: `CypherQueryHelper.getReturnPart(LabJournalEntryRevision.class)` projection. | XS | deferred | Audit §4 row 1. |
| OGM-HYDRATE-2026-05-24-002 | **OGM-HYDRATE-002** — `backend/.../timeseries/annotation/daos/TimeseriesAnnotationDAO.java`. Currently SAFE (uses `getReturnPart`) — flag against future "simplify the Cypher" refactor pressure that might inline the projection. Pin with a unit-test assertion + comment so the safety isn't accidentally removed. | XS | deferred | Audit §4 row 2. Tripwire, not a bug. |
| OGM-HYDRATE-2026-05-24-003 | **STRUCTURAL — custom SpotBugs/AST rule.** Fail the build on any Cypher `RETURN <leaf-only>` against a `@NodeEntity` that has at least one `@Relationship` field. Prevents the entire BUG-LJ-V1 defect class at PR time rather than chasing individual instances. Use SpotBugs detector + a regex-based `@NodeEntity`/`@Relationship` annotation scanner; emit High-confidence finding pointing at the offending Cypher string. | M | queued | Audit §6 + §7. Cheapest long-term insurance against this defect class. |
| OGM-HYDRATE-2026-05-24-004 | **Sibling sweep — service-layer composite-call hydration.** If a v2 service stitches two DAO returns and assumes `entityA.getEntityB()` is populated by the first call, the same NPE can fire even when both DAOs are individually correct. Out of scope for the DAO sweep; needs a separate audit pass over `de.dlr.shepard.v2.**.services.*`. Quick grep: any service method that calls one repository, then immediately walks `.getX().getY()` where Y wasn't projected. | S (audit only) | queued | Audit §5 sibling defect class. Defer until OGM-HYDRATE-001 deferred-row fires or a service-layer NPE surfaces. |

| WATCHED-COLLECTIONS-EMPTY-STATE | **"Watched collections feature seems gone" — likely silent-hide regression.** Code in `frontend/components/context/home/PersonalDigest.vue:198` reads `<template v-if="watched.length > 0 || watchedLoading">` — when the user has zero watched collections, the entire Watched section disappears (no header, no empty-state copy, no affordance to discover the binoculars-toggle). Fix: replace silent-hide with a helpful empty state ("You haven't watched any collections yet — open a collection and click the binoculars icon to add it"). Code is intact (`useWatchedCollections.ts` last changed 2 days ago, `c4f6e354`) — not a today-regression. Verify on live with a fresh / empty user account. | XS | queued | User-flagged 2026-05-24 evening. Same defect class as our other audit-derived "honest empty state" rule (per `feedback_basic_advanced_superset.md` + RDM-001 empty-state pattern). |
| AUTH-SESSION-AUTORENEW | **Auto-renew OIDC session instead of "Keep me signed in" checkbox.** User explicitly asked: silent token refresh as the default; remove the manual opt-in checkbox. Touch points: (a) NextAuth `[...].ts` configuration adds `session: { strategy: 'jwt', maxAge: ... }` + a refresh callback that hits Keycloak's `/protocol/openid-connect/token` with `grant_type=refresh_token` before access-token expiry; (b) Keycloak realm client config — set `Refresh Token Max Reuse` + ensure offline_access scope where appropriate; (c) frontend useAuth composable refresh-on-401 path (per existing UX rule `auto-refresh on stale session/cache`, task #49). Defaults: silent refresh; explicit "Sign out" still works; the existing "Keep me signed in" checkbox becomes a no-op or is removed. | M | queued | User-flagged 2026-05-24 evening. Pairs with task #49 (auto-refresh on stale session, completed). |

## UX-2026-05-24-* — collections + containers triage (UX scrutinizer findings)

SSOT: [`aidocs/agent-findings/ux-survey-collections-containers-2026-05-24.md`](agent-findings/ux-survey-collections-containers-2026-05-24.md). 4515-word audit + 24 Playwright screenshots + e2e reproducer spec. Three CRITICAL / multiple MAJOR findings at MFFD-scale (8514 DOs).

| ID | Item | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| UX-DOPANEL-STATUS-SERVER | **CRITICAL — push status filter to backend.** `CollectionDataObjectsPanel.vue:196-199` chip filter is applied client-side over only the 25 visible rows; clicking 'READY' on MFFD-Dropbox p.1 silently drops 800+ READY rows from remaining pages. Add a `status` query param to the list endpoint + apply server-side; remove the client-side filter. | M | queued | Audit Top 3 #1. Top urgency at MFFD scale. |
| UX-DOPANEL-TOTAL-COUNT | **MAJOR — add `Content-Range` header + "X-Y of N" + jump-to-page.** Today the DO panel paginates without showing total count or absolute position; researchers can't tell if they're on page 1 of 5 or page 1 of 343. Backend returns `Content-Range` (or `X-Total-Count`); frontend renders "Showing 1-25 of 8514" + page-input jump. | M | queued | Audit #2. |
| UX-ERR-STATE-COLLECTION-MISSING | **CRITICAL — empty-state branch for missing/deleted collection IDs.** `pages/collections/[collectionId]/index.vue:467` is `<CenteredLoadingSpinner v-else />` with no error branch — a bogus or soft-deleted appId hangs forever with 19 console errors per attempt. Add a `<NotFoundPanel />` branch for 404s on the collection fetch; same pattern for spatial container 404 (7 errors). | S | queued | Audit Top 3 #3. Same defect class as the WATCHED-COLLECTIONS-EMPTY-STATE silent-hide row above. |
| UX-PAGE-SHELL-RESPONSIVE-WIDTH | **MAJOR — single `<PageShell>` replacing 6 hard-clamp instances.** Six pages hard-clamp at 1200-1400px (CollectionListPage.vue:21, [collectionId]/index.vue:139, all four container detail pages). At 4K viewport this wastes 70%+ horizontal real estate and forces vertical scroll. New `<PageShell>` component with `max-width: min(1600px, 95vw)` + media-query breakpoints; replace all six callsites. | S | queued | Audit Top 3 #2. Pairs with `feedback_validate_user_viewport.md`. |
| UX-DATAOBJECT-MAP-LAZY | **MAJOR — stop eager `getAllDataObjects` XHR on every collection-detail mount.** `useFetchDataObjectMap.ts:9` fires an unbounded list call every page load just to populate a lab-journal name-lookup map; at MFFD-Dropbox (8514 DOs) this is one ~MB transfer + 200ms+ blocking parse per visit. Lazy-load: only fetch when the LJ panel opens; cache by collection-id + 5-minute TTL. | S | queued | Audit. Cousin of UI-020 (the bulk lab-journal endpoint shipped today) — same defect class, different consumer. |
| UX-LINEAGE-EMPTY-VS-NOEDGES | **MAJOR — `CollectionLineageGraph.vue:176` says 'No datasets in this collection' even when 17 DataObjects are visible 200px above.** Empty-state copy is wrong — it should distinguish (a) loading, (b) no DOs at all, (c) DOs exist but lineage is unwired (no Predecessor/Successor edges). Three different messages; the current code uses one for all three. | S | queued | Audit. Same defect class as several other "honest empty state" rows surfacing today. |
| UX-SPATIAL-VIEWER-OR-BANNER | **CRITICAL — spatial + video container pages are dead/missing.** `containers/spatialdata/[containerId]/index.vue` is title-only (70 lines, no payload viewer, no contents list) — placeholder indistinguishable from broken. `frontend/pages/containers/video/` DOES NOT EXIST entirely even though `CollectionDataObjectsPanel` renders video badges — clicking a video badge yields 404. Two paths: (a) ship the actual viewers (SPATIAL-V6-004 BrushTraceView for spatial; video viewer for video); (b) ship a clear "coming in SPATIAL-V6 / VID2" banner until then. | S (banners) + L (real viewers) | queued | Audit. Video-page absence is the headline — feature is referenced in nav but doesn't exist. |
| UX-SIDEBAR-COLLAPSE | **MAJOR — sidebar collapse toggle + dedupe "Add DataObject" buttons.** The collection-detail sidebar has no collapse affordance + "Add DataObject" appears twice (top action bar + sidebar). At narrower viewports this eats real estate; at 4K the sidebar is fine but the duplication is confusing. Add v-rail collapse + remove the duplicate button (keep the canonical position per `project_ui_modernization.md`). | S | queued | Audit. Sibling of #114 (existing `Fix sidebar rendering and usability`). |
| UX-LIST-VIRTUALIZATION | **MAJOR — virtual lists for 'Referenced by', LabJournal, channel-selector.** Each of these panels renders all N rows into the DOM today; at MFFD-Dropbox the Referenced-By panel has 1470 entries and the channel-selector on TR-001's TS container has hundreds. Use Vuetify `v-virtual-scroll` or TanStack Virtual; threshold N>50 swap to virtualized list. | M | queued | Audit. Same defect class as the v15.x graph-display concern (task #25). |
| UX-ROW-AS-LINK | **MINOR (high-impact UX) — wrap clickable rows in `<NuxtLink>` for middle-click + keyboard nav.** Tables use click-handler-on-row (`ContainerList.vue:111-122` + others); this breaks middle-click-to-open-in-new-tab + breaks keyboard accessibility (no tabindex/Enter). Wrap row contents in `<NuxtLink :to="...">` with `display: contents` styling; remove click handler; preserves all current behaviour + adds the missing affordances. | XS | queued | Audit. Cheap a11y + power-user UX win. |
| UX-OPS-AUTH-HELPER-TIMEOUT | **OPS — bump `loginAs` helper timeout from 10s → 30s.** `e2e/tests/helpers/auth.ts:90-104` post-submit SIGN OUT selector has 10s timeout; first-cold-login OIDC redirect chain takes 15-30s on the live system. Per `feedback_check_branch_before_merge.md` discipline — file as ops hygiene before next e2e dispatch. | XS | queued | Audit auth-blocker workaround note. |
| SEMA-V6-FUTURE-MULTI-SUBJECT | First-class multi-subject annotations via `:DefectGroup`-style intermediary | L | future (v2+) | §14 #8 |

## MFFD-INGEST-* — MFFD dump ingest prerequisites (2026-05-26)

Design ref: [`aidocs/data/108-mffd-dump-ingestion-plan.md`](data/108-mffd-dump-ingestion-plan.md). Five gaps must close before full MFFD import can proceed. Import is **deferred** until the functional prerequisites below are resolved. A metadata-only Phase 0 (CameraConfig INI + ProfileSet.tif + DO hierarchy) has no blockers and can proceed at any time.

| ID | Item | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| MFFD-TS-01 | **TimescaleDB pre-import chunk/partition as idempotent Flyway migration.** `backend/src/main/resources/db/migration/V1.13.0__Optimize_timeseries_chunk_config.sql` — sets chunk interval to 1 hour (vs default 7 days, wrong for sub-second sensor data) and adds 4 space partitions by `timeseries_id` (parallel ingestion). Both must be idempotent (`DO $$ IF NOT EXISTS ... $$`) since the hypertable may already have chunks. Without this, MFFD-scale ingest will create thousands of oversized 7-day chunks and suffer serial write contention. | S | **dispatched** | Dispatched 2026-05-26. Prerequisite for Phase 1 (FSD TS ingest). Pairs with P2b (CAgg). |
| MFFD-TS-02 | **INTEGRAL aggregation implementation.** Remove the `assertNotIntegral()` guard in `TimeseriesDataPointRepository.queryDataPoints()` and `queryAggregationFunction()` (`:462–464`). Implement two paths: (a) whole-range trapezoidal integral via native SQL `LAG()` window function — `SUM(0.5 × (v + v_next) × (t_next − t))` — returned as a single TimeseriesDataPoint; (b) time-bucketed midpoint approximation `AVG(v) × bucket_duration_ns` in `queryAggregationFunction` when a time-slice is set. Add unit tests + one integration test. Prerequisite for the welding energy budget analysis case (Case B in `aidocs/data/108`). | M | **dispatched** | Dispatched 2026-05-26. `AggregateFunction.INTEGRAL` already exists in the enum; the guard is the only blocker. |
| MFFD-IMPORT-01 | **MffdDumpSource — AFP 5-level hierarchy importer.** New class `de.dlr.shepard.v2.importer.sources.MffdDumpSource` extending the v16 importer to understand the AFP Run → PlyGroup → Layup → Layer → Track directory tree. Per-track: parse CameraConfig INI for DataObject attributes (track number, ply, length, tow width, start/stop ns), route FSDSet.csv to TimeseriesContainer using `ChronoTimeInUs × 1000` as ns timestamp, route PointCloud.csv to FileReference (or SpatialContainer once SP1 lands), route ProfileSet.tif to FileContainer (Garage S3), route ProfileSet.csv (brush data) to StructuredDataContainer. Skip 0-byte OID payloads gracefully (note `payload_available: false` attribute). | L | queued | Gated on MFFD-TS-01 (chunk migration) + MFFD-TS-02 (INTEGRAL, needed for FSD ingest correctness check). SP1 (#79) gating for PointCloud — fallback to FileReference acceptable for Phase 1. |
| MFFD-BATCH-01 | **Bulk DataObject creation endpoint — `POST /v2/data-objects/batch`.** Accepts a JSON array of DataObject creation requests (up to 500 per call). Returns a 207 Multi-Status body with per-item status + created appId. Needed because MFFD imports 17,600+ DataObjects; at 1 DO/s with 4 workers the AFP tapelaying step takes 1–2 hours — a batch endpoint reduces this 10–100×. Include permission check (caller must have write on all parent collections) and PROV-O batch writeback. | M | queued | Independent of MFFD-TS series. High value for any large-dataset import scenario (LUMEN + future). |
| MFFD-JOIN-01 | **Design: scan-line join key across TPS stores.** The `Packet` index (0-based integer) is the shared row key across FSDSet, PointCloud, ProfileSet.tif, and BrushData for each AFP track. Today Shepard has no first-class way to express "row N in TS container A = row N in SpatialContainer B." Design options: (a) store `Packet` as an additional TS channel and expose it in the multi-channel endpoint (TS-OPT2, #226); (b) rely on absolute timestamp alignment (`ChronoTimeInUs × 1000` in FSD = wall-clock ns for TimescaleDB) and assume the spatial data is co-registered at the same ns timestamps; (c) add a `frame_index` column to SpatialContainer. Option (b) is sufficient for Phase 1 if FSD timestamps are used consistently in both stores. | S (design) | queued | No implementation until Phase 2 (PointCloud/spatial). Design note can land as aidocs without code. |
| MFFD-NDRIVE-01 | **N: drive mount on DLR cube for scripted ingest.** Set up persistent mount of `\\bt-au-freenas1.intra.dlr.de\share\Messdaten\` (or the NAS path confirmed by DLR infra) on the DLR cube host. Required for Phase 7 (FSD/PointCloud backfill from N: drive), MFFD-PARSER-SVDX1 (SVDX welding TS), and §6.3 video ingest. User confirmed N: drive accessible from DLR systems 2026-05-26. Operations task — no code changes in shepard; config-managed via cube ansible/runbook. | S (ops) | queued | Confirmed accessible (2026-05-26). Contact: DLR Augsburg infra team. Document mount path in the MFFD ingest runbook once confirmed. |
| MFFD-PARSER-01 | **`FileParserPlugin` SPI skeleton — post-upload async enrichment hook.** Define `FileParserPlugin` interface, `ParseCapability` record, `ParseContext` + `ParseResult` types, `FileParserRegistry` CDI bean, `ParseJob` persisted via `JobService`. Trigger: `FileContainerService.upload()` calls `FileParserRegistry.findParser()` after OID creation; match returns async `ParseJob`. Status queryable via `GET /v2/file-containers/{fcId}/files/{oid}/parse-status`. Design doc: `aidocs/integrations/110`. | M | queued | Prerequisite for MFFD-PARSER-SA1 + MFFD-PARSER-SVDX1. Distinct from `shepard-plugin-importer` (cross-instance vs post-upload). |
| MFFD-PARSER-SA1 | **`shepard-plugin-parser-sa` — Spatial Analyzer `.xit`/`.xit64` parser.** Implements `FileParserPlugin` for NRK Spatial Analyzer format. Reads binary header to detect `measurementType` (DISCRETE_POINTS vs 6D_PROBE_SCAN). Routes: discrete point groups → StructuredDataContainer rows `(pointName, x, y, z, spatialRms)`; 6D probe streams → TimeseriesContainer channels `(x, y, z, roll, pitch, yaw)` at kHz rates. Stamps DataObject attrs: `instrument.type = "Leica AT901"`, `frame_of_reference`. Design doc: `aidocs/integrations/110 §4.1`. | L | queued | Gated on MFFD-PARSER-01 (SPI skeleton). Blocked until test `.xit` file procured — contact DLR ZLP metrology team. |
| MFFD-PARSER-SVDX1 | **`shepard-plugin-parser-svdx` — Beckhoff TwinCAT Scope `.svdx` → TimescaleDB.** Implements `FileParserPlugin` for `.svdx` / TDMS format. Wraps existing `tdms2csv.py` (in `tool_sources/`) as subprocess or ports logic to Java. Output: one TimeseriesContainer per file; channel names from SVDX header; DataObject attrs `process.type = "welding"`, `weld.seam_id` from filename. Volume: 181 SVDX files × 20 channels × ~30k points. Design doc: `aidocs/integrations/110 §4.2`. | M | queued | Gated on MFFD-PARSER-01 + MFFD-NDRIVE-01 (files on N: drive). |
